§ 10.01 TITLE OF CODE.
   All ordinances of a permanent and general nature of the city, as revised,
codified, rearranged, renumbered and consolidated into component codes, titles,
chapters and sections, shall be known and designated as the “City of Hartford
City Code,” for which the designation “code of ordinances,” “codified
ordinances” or “code” may be substituted. Code title, chapter and section
headings do not constitute any part of the law as contained in the code.
§ 10.02 INTERPRETATION.
   Unless otherwise provided herein or by law or implication required, the same
rules of construction, definition and application shall govern the
interpretation of this code as those governing the interpretation of state law.
§ 10.03 CONSTRUING PROVISIONS.
   The provisions of the ordinances of the city, and all proceedings under
them, are to be construed with a view to effect their objects and to promote
justice.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.080)
§ 10.04 APPLICATION TO FUTURE ORDINANCES.
   All provisions of Title I compatible with future legislation shall apply to
ordinances hereafter adopted which amend or supplement this code, unless
otherwise specifically provided.
§ 10.05 CONSTRUCTION OF CODE.
   (A)   This code is a codification of previously- existing laws, amendments
thereto and newly-enacted laws. Any previously-existing law or amendment
thereto reenacted by this code shall continue in operation and effect as if it
had not been repealed by this code. All rules and regulations adopted under
laws reenacted in this code shall remain in full force and effect unless
repealed or amended subsequent to the enactment of this code.
   (B)   Any appropriation repealed and reenacted by this code is continued
only for the period designated in the original enactment of that appropriation.
   (C)   The numerical order and position of sections in this code does not
resolve a conflict between two or more sections.
   (D)   Any irreconcilable conflict between sections shall be resolved by
reference to the dates that the sections were originally enacted. The section
most recently enacted supersedes any conflicting section or division.
   (E)   All references within a section of this code to any section of
previously-existing laws refer to the numbers in the original enactment.
   (F)   (1)   The numerical designations and descriptive headings assigned to
the various titles, chapters, subchapters and sections of this code, whether as
originally enacted or as added by amendment, are not law and may be altered by
the compilers of this or any subsequent codification in any official
publication to more clearly indicate its content. These descriptive headings
are for organizational purposes only and do not affect the meaning, application
or construction of the law they precede.
      (2)   Each note following a section of this code is for reference
purposes only and is not a part of the section.
   (G)   All references to any section of this code refer to all subsequent
amendments to that section unless otherwise provided.
(I.C. 1-1-1-5)
§ 10.06 RULES OF INTERPRETATION; DEFINITIONS.
   (A)   Rules of interpretation. This code shall be construed by the following
rules unless the construction is plainly repugnant to the legislative intent or
context of the provision.
      (1)   Words and phrases shall be taken in their plain, ordinary and usual
sense. Technical words and phrases having a peculiar and appropriate meaning in
law shall be understood according to their technical import.
      (2)   Words imputing joint authority to three or more persons shall be
construed as imputing authority to a majority of the persons unless otherwise
declared in the section giving the authority.
      (3)   Where a section requires an act to be done which, by law, an agent
or deputy may perform in addition to the principal, the performance of the act
by an authorized deputy or agent is valid.
      (4)   Words denoting the masculine gender shall be deemed to include the
feminine and neuter genders. Words in the singular shall include the plural and
words in the plural shall include the singular. The use of a verb in the
present tense shall include the past and future tenses and vice versa, unless
manifestly inapplicable.
   (B)   Definitions. For the purpose of this code of ordinances, the following
definitions apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different
meaning.
      BASIC CATV SERVICE. The distribution of broadcast television signals by
the company.
      CABLE TELEVISION SYSTEM or CATV. A system composed of, without
limitation, antennas, cables, wires, lines, towers, wave guides or any other
conductors, converters, equipment or facilities designed, constructed or wired
for the purpose of producing visual, radio, television, electronic or
electrical signals to and from persons, subscribers and locations in the
franchise area.
      CITY. The City of Hartford City, Indiana, or the area within the
territorial limits outside of the city over which the city has jurisdiction or
control by virtue of any constitutional or statutory provisions.
      CLERK-TREASURER. The Clerk- Treasurer of the Common Council.
      COMPANY. The grantee of rights under an ordinance.
      COUNCIL. The Common Council of the City of Hartford City, Indiana.
      COUNTY. The County of Blackford, Indiana.
      ECONOMICAL. An improvement, expansion or maintenance of the sendee at the
same or less cost to the customer of the company.
      FRANCHISE AREA. The area within the corporate limits of the city.
      GALLERY. Any building, room or combination of buildings and rooms for the
specific purpose of displaying or creating visual arts.
      GROSS ANNUAL BASIC SUBSCRIBER REVENUES. Any and all compensation and
other consideration received directly by the company from subscribers in
payment for regularly-furnished basic CATV service. GROSS ANNUAL BASIC
SUBSCRIBER REVENUE shall not include any taxes on services furnished by the
company which are imposed directly on any subscriber or user by any city, state
or other governmental unit and collected by the company for the governmental
unit.
      HIGHWAY. Includes bridges, roads and streets, unless otherwise expressly
provided.
      LAW. Denotes applicable federal law, the constitution, the statutes of
the state, the ordinances of the city and, when appropriate, any and all rules
and regulations which may be promulgated thereunder.
      LITERARY ARTS. Any written form including, but not limited to, creative
writing projects, poetry, fiction, non-fiction, short stories, plays or
dramatic writing.
      MAY. The act referred to is permissive.
      MONTH. One calendar month.
      MUST and SHALL. The acts referred to are each mandatory.
      OATH. Includes an affirmation or declaration in all cases in which, by
law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in those cases, the
words “swear” and “sworn” shall be equivalent to the words “affirm” and
“affirmed.”
      OWNER. Applied to a building or land, includes any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or tenant by the entirety of the whole or
a part of the building or land.
      PERFORMING ARTS. Any art form recognized as a performing art, such as
dramatic presentations, dance, folk dance, ballet or any other art form
commonly recognized as a PERFORMING ART.
      PERSON. Includes a natural person, joint venture, association, club,
joint stock company, partnership, company, corporation, business, trust or
organization or the manager, lessee, agent, servant, officer or employee of any
of them.
      PERSONAL PROPERTY. Includes money, goods, chattels, things in action and
evidences of debt.
      PRECEDING and FOLLOWING. Next before and next after, respectively.
      PROPERTY. Includes real property and personal property.
      PROPERTY OF COMPANY. All property owned, installed or used by the company
in the conduct of a CATV business in the city.
      REAL PROPERTY. Includes lands, tenements and hereditaments.
      SIDEWALK. The portion of a street between the curb line and the adjacent
property line which is intended for the use of pedestrians.
      STATE. The State of Indiana.
      STREET. Includes all streets, highways, avenues, lanes, alleys, courts,
places, squares, curbs or other public ways in the city which have been or may
hereafter be dedicated and opened to public use or other public property so
designated in any law of the state.
      SUBSCRIBER. Any person or entity receiving basic CATV service.
      TENANT and OCCUPANT. Applied to a building or land, includes any person
who occupies the whole or part of the building or land, whether alone or with
others.
      THEATER. Any building, room or collection of rooms designed and
specifically employed for the purpose of the display and creative use of the
performing arts, including rehearsals, castings, backdrops, scenery and
audience facilities.
      VISUAL ARTS. Any art form recognized as a visual art, including painting,
sculpture, ceramics or any other commonly-recognized art form requiring visual
appreciation.
      WRITTEN or IN WRITING. Includes printed, typewritten, mimeographed,
multi-graphed or otherwise reproduced in permanent visible form. Where the
written signature of a person is required, the terms mean the proper
handwriting of the person or the person’s mark.
      YEAR. One calendar year unless otherwise expressly provided.
(I.C. 1-1-4-5) (Prior Code, § 1.04.010)
§ 10.07 SEVERABILITY.
   (A)   If any section of this code now enacted or subsequently amended or its
application to any person or circumstance is held invalid, then the invalidity
does not affect other sections which can be given effect without the invalid
section or application.
   (B)   Except in the case of a section or amendment to this code containing a
nonseverability provision, each division or part of every section is severable.
If any portion or application of a section is held invalid, then the invalidity
does not affect the remainder of the section unless:
      (1)   The remainder is so essentially and inseparably connected with and
so dependent upon the invalid provision or application that it cannot be
presumed that the remainder would have been enacted without the invalid
provision or application; or
      (2)   The remainder is incomplete and incapable of being executed in
accordance with the legislative intent without the invalid provision or
application.
   (C)   This section applies to every section of this code regardless of
whether a section was enacted before or after the passage of this code.
   (D)   The repeal of a section or amendment stating that the provisions of a
chapter, subchapter or section are severable as provided in division (B) above
does not affect the operation of division (B) above with respect to that
chapter, subchapter or section.
(I.C. 1-1-1-8)
§ 10.08 REFERENCE TO OTHER SECTIONS.
   Whenever in one section reference is made to another section hereof, the
reference shall extend and apply to the section referred to as subsequently
amended, revised, recodified or renumbered unless the subject matter is changed
or materially altered by the amendment or revision.
§ 10.09 REFERENCE TO OFFICES; NAME DESIGNATIONS.
   (A)   Reference to offices. Reference to a public office or officer shall be
deemed to apply to any office, officer or employee of the municipality who is
exercising the powers, duties or functions contemplated in a provision
irrespective of any transfer of functions or change in the official title of
the functionary.
   (B)   Name designations. Whenever any ordinance or resolution of the Council
refers to any board, bureau, commission, division, department, officer, agency,
authority or instrumentality of any government and that name designation is
incorrectly stated, on the effective date of that ordinance or following the
effective date, the rights, powers, duties or liabilities placed with that
entity are or were transferred to a different entity, then the named board,
bureau, commission, department, division, officer, agency, authority or
instrumentality, whether correctly named in the ordinance at its effective date
or not, means that correctly-named entity or the entity to which the duties,
liabilities, powers and rights were transferred.
(I.C. 1-1-6-1)
§ 10.10 ERRORS AND OMISSIONS.
   (A)   If a manifest error is discovered consisting of the misspelling of any
words, the omission of any word or words necessary to express the intent of the
provisions affected, the use of a word or words to which no meaning can be
attached or the use of a word or words when another word or words was clearly
intended to express the intent, then the spelling shall be corrected and the
word or words supplied, omitted or substituted as will conform with the
manifest intention, and the provisions shall have the same effect as though the
correct words were contained in the text as originally published.
   (B)   No alteration shall be made or permitted if any question exists
regarding the nature or extent of the error.
§ 10.11 PROHIBITED ACTS INCLUDE CAUSING AND PERMITTING.
   Whenever, in the ordinances of the city, any act or omission is made
unlawful, it shall include causing, allowing, permitting, abiding, abetting,
suffering or concealing the fact of the act or omission.
(Prior Code, § 1.04.060)
§ 10.12 REASONABLE TIME.
   (A)   In all cases where an ordinance requires an act to be done in a
reasonable time or requires reasonable notice to be given, REASONABLE TIME OR
NOTICE shall be deemed to mean the time which is necessary for a prompt
performance of the act or giving of the notice.
   (B)   The time within which an act is to be done, as herein provided, shall
be computed by excluding the first day and including the last. If the last day
be a Sunday or a state holiday, then it shall be excluded.
§ 10.13 REPEAL OR MODIFICATION OF CODE SECTION.
   When a section of this code which repealed a former section or law adopted
prior to the enactment of this code is repealed, the former section or law is
not revived unless it so expressly provides. The repeal of any section shall
not extinguish or release any penalty, forfeiture or liability incurred under
the section unless the repealing section so expressly provides. The section
shall be treated as still remaining in force for the purpose of sustaining any
proper action or prosecution for the enforcement of the penalty, forfeiture or
liability.
(I.C. 1-1-5-1)
§ 10.14 LIMITATION PERIODS.
   The running of any period of limitations or any requirement of notice
contained in any law, whether applicable to civil causes or proceedings, to the
prosecution of offenses or for the recovery of penalties and forfeitures, which
are repealed and reenacted by this code shall not be affected by the repeal and
reenactment, but all suits, proceedings and prosecutions for causes arising or
acts committed prior to the effective date of this code may be commenced and
prosecuted with the same effect as if this code had not been enacted.
Statutory reference:
   Periods of limitation, see I.C. 1-1-1-7
§ 10.15 ORDINANCES UNAFFECTED.
   All ordinances of a temporary or special nature and all other ordinances
pertaining to subjects not embraced in this code shall remain in full force and
effect unless herein repealed expressly or by necessary implication.
§ 10.16 ORDINANCES WHICH AMEND OR SUPPLEMENT CODE.
   (A)   If the legislative body shall desire to amend any existing chapter or
section of this code, then the chapter or section shall be specifically
repealed and a new chapter or section containing the desired amendment
substituted in its place.
   (B)   Any ordinance which is proposed to add to the existing code a new
chapter or section shall indicate, with reference to the arrangement of this
code, the proper number of the chapter or section. In addition to an indication
thereof as may appear in the text of the proposed ordinance, a caption or title
shall be shown in concise form above the ordinance.
§ 10.17 SECTION HISTORIES; STATUTORY REFERENCES.
   (A)   As histories for the code sections, the specific number and passage
date of the original ordinances and amending ordinances, if any, are listed
following the text of the code section. Example:
(Ord. 10, passed 5-13-1960; Ord. 15, passed 1-1-1970; Ord. 20, passed 1-1-1980;
Ord. 25, passed 1-1-1985)
   (B)   (1)   If a statutory cite is included in the history, then this
indicates that the text of the section reads substantially the same as the
statute. Example:
(I.C. 36-5-2-2)
      (2)   If a statutory cite is set forth as a “statutory reference”
following the text of the section, then this indicates that the reader should
refer to that statute for further information. Example:
         § 39.01 PUBLIC RECORDS AVAILABLE.
            This municipality shall make available to any person for inspection
or copying all public records unless otherwise exempted by state law.
         Statutory reference:
            Inspection of public records, see I.C. 5-14-3-1 et seq.
   (C)   If a section of this code is derived from the previous code of
ordinances of the city published in a previous year and subsequently amended,
the previous code section number shall be indicated in the history by “(Prior
Code, §      ).”
§ 10.18 PRESERVATION OF PENALTIES, OFFENSES, RIGHTS AND LIABILITIES.
   (A)   All offenses committed under laws in force prior to the effective date
of this code shall be prosecuted and remain punishable as provided by those
laws.
   (B)   (1)   This code does not affect any rights or liabilities accrued,
penalties incurred or proceedings begun prior to the effective date of this
code. The liabilities, proceedings and rights are continued and the
punishments, penalties and forfeitures enforced and imposed as if this code had
not been enacted.
      (2)   In particular, any agreement granting permission to utilize highway
rights-of-way, contracts entered into, franchises granted, the acceptance,
establishment or vacation of any highway and the election of corporate officers
shall remain valid in all respects as if this code had not been enacted.
§ 10.99 GENERAL PENALTY.
   Any person violating any of the provisions or failing to comply with any of
the mandatory requirements of the ordinances of the city shall be guilty of an
offense. Except in cases where a different punishment is prescribed by any
ordinance of the city, any person convicted of an offense shall be punished by
a fine of up to $7,500, except for violations of ordinances regulating traffic
and parking.
(Prior Code, § 1.08.010)
CHAPTER 11: CITY STANDARDS
Section
   
11.01   Boundaries adopted by reference
§ 11.01 BOUNDARIES ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   The city’s official map is hereby adopted by reference and made a part of
this chapter as fully as if the same were attached hereto and incorporated
herein, and such is on public display in City Hall and filed with the offices
of the County Auditor and County Recorder. The map specifies the corporation
boundaries of the city.
(Prior Code, § 11.04.010)

EXECUTIVE BRANCH
§ 30.01 MAYOR.
   (A)   Establishment and powers. The Mayor is the city’s executive and the
head of the executive branch. He or she shall faithfully perform the duties and
responsibilities as set forth in I.C. 36-4-5 and all other applicable statutes
of the state.
   (B)   Term of office. The term of office of the Mayor is four years,
beginning at noon on the January 1 after his or her election and continuing
until a successor is elected and qualified.
   (C)   Election. The Mayor shall be elected by voters of the whole city.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.010) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.02 BOARD OF PUBLIC WORKS AND SAFETY.
   (A)   Establishment and powers. There is hereby established a Board of
Public Works and Safety within the executive branch. The Board shall be the
chief administrative body of the city and shall have control of the day-to-day
operations of the executive departments established in §
30.03 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.020)
   (B)   Members of the Board and powers.
      (1)   The members of the Board of Public Works and Safety shall consist
of the Mayor and two residents of the city, who shall be chosen by the Mayor
and serve at his or her pleasure. The Board of Public Works and Safety shall
exercise the powers and duties as prescribed by state law.
      (2)   The Mayor is specifically authorized to choose members of the Board
of Public Works and Safety, shall appoint the heads of the departments listed
in §
30.03 of this chapter and shall appoint the head of the Department of Parks and
Recreation with the approval of the Board operating the Department, pursuant to
I.C. 36-4-9-2 and I.C. 36-4-11-2.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.030)
(Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.03 ESTABLISHMENT OF EXECUTIVE DEPARTMENTS.
   (A)   The following executive departments are hereby established:
      (1)   Police Department;
      (2)   Fire Department;
      (3)   Street Department;
      (4)   Waterworks Utility Department;
      (5)   Sewage Works Department; and
      (6)   Department of Law, established pursuant to I.C. 36-4-9-12.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.020)
   (B)   The departments established in division (A) above shall perform the
administrative functions assigned to them by statute and ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.040)
(Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984; Res. 1992-34, passed 10-19-1992)
§ 30.04 PURCHASING DEPARTMENT.
   (A)   Establishment. There is established the Purchasing Department of the
city, which shall be subject to applicable provisions of the state statutes and
any subsequent or amending statutes.
   (B)   Purchasing Agent.
      (1)   (a)   There is established the position of Purchasing Agent for the
city.
         (b)   The Purchasing Agent shall be appointed by the Mayor and shall
serve at the pleasure of the Mayor.
      (2)   The Purchasing Agent shall be compensated at a salary established
in a salary ordinance by the Common Council of the city and provided within a
budget ordinance adopted by the Common Council of the city.
   (C)   Duties, responsibilities and administration. The duties,
responsibilities and methods of administration of the Purchasing Department of
the city shall conform with those delineated in I.C. 5-22 and by the Board of
Public Works and Safety of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.070) (Ord. 1059, passed 7-17-1985)
§ 30.05 POWERS OF DEPARTMENTS.
   Subject to the appropriation power of the Common Council, the departments in
§§
30.03 and
30.04 of this chapter shall have the ability to hire employees and purchase or
contract for materials and services as the Board of Public Works and Safety or
other governing boards or commissions deem necessary in order for the
departments to perform their public functions.
(Prior Code, § 2.24.050) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
LEGISLATIVE BRANCH
§ 30.20 COMMON COUNCIL, COMPOSITION AND TERM.
   (A)   Establishment and powers. The legislative branch of the city is the
Common Council. The Common Council shall have exclusive authority to adopt
ordinances, appropriate tax monies received by the city and perform the duties
prescribed by I.C. 36-4-6.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.010)
   (B)   Membership. The Council shall be comprised of five members, four of
whom are elected from distinct districts and one of whom is elected by the
voters of the city at large. Redistricting of councilmanic districts shall be
done every ten years in accordance to I.C. 36-4-6-4 and 36-4-6-5.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.050)
   (C)   Term of office. The term of office for a Common Council member is four
years, beginning at noon on the January 1 after his or her election and
continuing until a successor is elected and qualified.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.060)
(Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.21 PRESIDING OFFICER OF THE COMMON COUNCIL.
   Pursuant to the applicable statutes of I.C. 36-4-6-10 through 36-4-6-17, the
Mayor, or in the absence of the Mayor, the President of the Common Council,
shall be the presiding officer of the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.040) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.22 CLERK OF THE COMMON COUNCIL.
   The Clerk-Treasurer shall be the Clerk of the Council and shall perform
duties prescribed by I.C. 36-4-6-9 and other duties as the Council may direct.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.020) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.23 COMMON COUNCIL MEETINGS.
   The regular meeting for the Common Council of the city shall be held at 7:30
p.m. on the first Monday of each month in the Council’s chambers with the
exception of the first Monday in September, which meeting shall be held at that
hour and place on the last Monday in August.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.030) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.24 COMMON COUNCIL PROCEDURES.
   (A)   No person shall use violent or contemptuous language, behave in a
disorderly manner or otherwise refuse to obey the orders of the Mayor or
presiding officer in the Council’s chambers while the Common Council is in
session. The Mayor or presiding officer may order the removal from the
Council’s chambers of any person who intentionally disturbs the decorum of a
meeting.
   (B)   All ordinances except for budget ordinances and zoning ordinances of
the city shall require not more than two consecutive meetings, and all
ordinances in conflict hereof are hereby repealed.
   (C)   Resolutions may be passed on the same day on which they are introduced
upon receiving the approval of at least three of five members of the Common
Council.
   (D)   On the passage or adoption of any ordinance or resolution, the yeas
and nays shall be taken and entered in the record, and an ordinance shall be
processed in accordance with I.C. 36-4-6-14 through 36-4-6-17.
   (E)   All ordinances presented for passage by the Council may be read by
title only if, prior to the introduction of any ordinance, the ordinance has
been made available to all Council members, the press and the public for study.
At the introduction of an ordinance and upon a motion duly adopted, the
ordinance shall be read by title and discussion called for by Council members,
and then the introduction for each reading and, upon the discussion being
closed, motion and vote upon the ordinance shall be taken by the Council. Any
decision to suspend the rules governing the passage of an ordinance or
resolution can only be made by unanimous vote of the Council when at least four
members are in attendance.
   (F)   Any abstention from voting by a Council member shall constitute a nay
vote, except for in the case of an abstention for a declared reason of conflict
of interest.
(Prior Code, § 2.28.040) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984; Ord. 1274, passed 11-20-
1989)
§ 30.25 ELECTION OF COMMON COUNCIL MEMBERS.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      CITY. The City of Hartford City, Indiana.
      COUNCIL. The Common Council of the city.
      PRECINCT. The precinct by that name, as established by the County Board
of Commissioners and approved by the State Election Board under I.C. 3-11-1.5,
which is in existence on the effective date of this section.      
(Prior Code, § 2.16.010)
   (B)   Voting for Council members. The Council is composed of five members.
Each voter of the city may vote for one candidate for at-large membership and
for one candidate from the district in which the voter resides.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.020)
   (C)   Council districts. The Council divides the city into districts for the
purpose of conducting elections of Council members. See Exhibit “A,” which is
attached to the ordinance codified herein and made a part hereof by reference
as if set out herein in full.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.030)
   (D)   Areas not included in a district. If any part of the city is not
included in one of the districts established by division (C) above, then that
territory is included within the district which:
      (1)   Is contiguous to that territory; and
      (2)   Contains the smallest population, as “population” is defined in
I.C. 1-1-4-5.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.040)
   (E)   Areas in more than one district. If any part of the city is included
in more than one of the districts established by division (C) above, then that
territory is included within the district which:
      (1)   Is one of the districts in which the territory is described in
division (C) above;
      (2)   Is contiguous to that territory; and
      (3)   Contains the smallest population, as “population” is defined in
I.C. 1-1-4-5.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.050)
   (F)   Adoption of map.
      (1)   The Council adopts a map depicting the districts established under
division (C) above and incorporates said map by reference into this division
(F). Two copies of this map are on file in the office of the Clerk-Treasurer
for public inspection as required by I.C. 36-1-5-4.
      (2)   If a conflict exists between the districts as depicted on the map
and as described in division (C) above, then the description in division (C)
prevails.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.060)
   (G)   County Election Board notification. The Clerk-Treasurer of the city
forwarded a signed copy of this section to the Circuit Court Clerk of the
county and requested the Clerk to include the copy of this section in the
records of the County Election Board.
(Prior Code, § 2.16.070)
FISCAL BRANCH
§ 30.40 CITY CLERK-TREASURER, ELECTION AND TERM.
   (A)   Establishment and powers. The Clerk-Treasurer is the Fiscal Officer of
the city and the head of the fiscal branch. He or she shall perform the duties
assigned by I.C. 36-4-10 and other duties as the Common Council may require by
ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.010)
   (B)   Election. The Clerk-Treasurer shall be elected by the voters of the
whole city.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.020)
   (C)   Term of office. The term of office of the Clerk-Treasurer is four
years, beginning at noon on the January 1 after his or her election and
continuing until a successor is elected and qualified.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.030)
(Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.41 DEPUTY CLERK-TREASURER.
   The Clerk-Treasurer is hereby authorized, pursuant to I.C. 36-4-11-4, to
appoint one Deputy Clerk-Treasurer, who is to be paid solely from funds
appropriated for the office of the Clerk-Treasurer. The Deputy shall work under
the exclusive direction of the Clerk-Treasurer and serve at the pleasure of the
Clerk-Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.040) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
§ 30.42 CITY UTILITY ADMINISTRATION.
   (A)   (1)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall furnish space within his or her office
for the administration and records of the city’s utilities.
      (2)   The various utility clerks needed to manage the bookkeeping and
administrative requirements of said utilities shall be appointed after
recommendation to the Board by the Clerk-Treasurer, and after employment, shall
be compensated by the Board having control of the utility which the utility
clerk serves.
   (B)   (1)   The Clerk-Treasurer is authorized and made responsible for the
immediate supervision and discipline of the utility clerk(s) and payroll clerk
(s).
      (2)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall supervise the performance and duties of
the utility clerk(s) and payroll clerk(s).
   (C)   (1)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall abide by the procedures established by
the Board of Public Works and Safety, the Common Council, the applicable
provisions of the State Code and the applicable provisions of the United States
Code in the performance of his or her disciplinary and supervision duties and
in recommending the dismissal of employees.
      (2)   The utility clerk(s) and payroll clerk(s) are at-will employees and
may be dismissed by the Board of Public Works and Safety under the conditions
of at-will employment upon the recommendation of the Clerk-Treasurer and the
concurrence of the Board of Public Works and Safety.
   (D)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall be compensated for services which he or she
renders to the city’s utilities.
(Prior Code, § 2.36.050) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984; Ord. 1136, passed 12-8-
1986; Ord. 2003-17, passed 12-1-2003)
JUDICIAL BRANCH
§ 30.55 ABOLITION OF THE CITY COURT.
   Ord. 1036 and Ord. 1095, which were adopted by the Common Council January 5,
1984, and August 7, 1985, respectively, are hereby repealed and the City Court
is hereby abolished.
(Prior Code, § 2.40.010)
Editor’s note:
   The City Court was abolished by Ord. 1136, passed 12-8-1986.
§ 30.56 ENABLING PROVISIONS.
   The Clerk-Treasurer of the city shall notify the Clerk of the County
Election Board of the provisions of this subchapter and that there will be no
election for the office of City Judge in 1987 due to the abolition of the City
Court. The Clerk-Treasurer shall inform and notify the Secretary of the State,
the Judge of the County Circuit Court and the State Court Administrator at the
State Supreme Court that the City Court has been abolished and of the effective
date of said abolition.
(Prior Code, § 2.40.020)
§ 30.57 TRANSFER OF JURISDICTION.
   (A)   Upon the abolition of the City Court, on the effective date of the
abolition of the City Court, all matters then pending, all records of
proceedings, findings or judgments and docket books and records of cases closed
or pending, together with all pertinent findings and the like, shall be
transferred to the custody of the County Court.
   (B)   Henceforward, from the aforesaid date, the County Court shall have
full jurisdiction over all complaints for violations of city ordinances and
shall be the authorized court of record for the pleadings and processes which
are necessitated by the proper conducting of city business and enforcement of
city ordinances. The City Attorney shall cause all city pleadings for the
enforcement of city ordinances to be filed and heard before the County Superior
Court following the penalties collected by the County Superior Court as a
result of findings in city ordinance violations shall be forwarded, at least
monthly, to the City Clerk-Treasurer to be deposited in the City General Fund.
   (C)   The Judge of the City Court, prior to the effective date of the
abolition of the Court, shall cause all financial ledgers and records of the
Court to be transferred to the custody of the City Clerk-Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 2.40.030)
§ 30.58 STATUTORY AUTHORITY AND EFFECTIVE DATE.
   This subchapter was specifically adopted pursuant to the authority vested in
the Common Council by state statutes, and took effect at 11:59 p.m., EST, on
December 31, 1987.
(Prior Code, § 2.40.040)
§ 30.59 CONTINUATION OF CITY COURT OPERATION REQUIRED AND AUTHORIZED UNTIL 12-
31-1987.
   (A)   The Judge, Clerk and Bailiff of the City Court shall continue to cause
the City Court to be in full operation until December 31, 1987, and shall
continue to be compensated at the level of remuneration established by
ordinance.
   (B)   Should the City Court Judge, Clerk or Bailiff for any reason cease to
perform their duties in a manner required to maintain City Court operations
prior to December 31, 1987, or fail to assist in the transition and transfer of
jurisdiction to the County Court, then the Common Council shall, by resolution,
make a finding of nonperformance of duties in each case and prohibit the
payment of any further remuneration to the person or persons failing to perform
duties.
(Prior Code, § 2.40.050) (Ord. 1136, passed 12-8-1986)

GENERAL ORGANIZATIONS
§ 31.001 POLICE PENSION BOARD OF TRUSTEES.
   There shall be a Police Pension Board of Trustees to perform certain duties
prescribed by I.C. 36-8-6, 1925 fund, and I.C. 36-8-8, 1977 fund, concerning
the statutory pension of city police officers.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.020)
§ 31.002 FIREFIGHTERS’ PENSION BOARD OF TRUSTEES.
   There shall be a Firefighters’ Pension Board of Trustees to perform certain
duties prescribed by I.C. 36-8-7, 1925 fund, and I.C. 36-8-8, 1977 fund,
concerning the statutory pension of city firefighters.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.030)
§ 31.003 COUNTY AREA PLAN COMMISSION.
   (A)   The Common Council hereby adopts the provisions of Ch. 138 of the Acts
of the 1957 State General Assembly, as amended, I.C. 36-4 et seq.
   (B)   The city hereby agrees to join in and participate with the Area
Planning Department of the county, which was established by a separate
ordinance of the county, and which was organized at its first meeting called by
the President of the Board of County Commissions.
   (C)   The membership of the County Area Planning Commission shall be set
forth in I.C. 36-7-4 et seq.
   (D)   Upon its passage and proper signature, a copy of this section was
certified to the Board of County Commissioners of the county, the respective
officials of the City of Montpelier, Indiana, and the President of the Board of
County Commissioners.
(Prior Code, § 2.12.010) (Ord. 741, passed 5-20-1986)
STORM WATER MANAGEMENT DEPARTMENT
§ 31.015 ESTABLISHMENT.
   The city adopted the provisions of I.C. 8-1.5-5, thereby creating a
Department of Storm Water Management.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.010)
§ 31.016 BOARD OF DIRECTORS; POWERS AND DUTIES.
   (A)   The Department of Storm Water Management shall be controlled by the
Board of Directors, consisting of three Directors who are members of the City
Board of Public Works.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.020)
   (B)   The Board shall have the powers and duties prescribed by I.C. 8-1.5-3-
4(a) and may, in addition, hold hearings following public notice, make findings
and determinations, install, maintain and operate a storm water collection and
disposal system, make all necessary or desirable improvements of the grounds
and premises under its control and issue and sell bonds of the district in the
name of the municipality for the acquisition, construction, alteration,
addition or extension of the storm water collection and disposal system or for
the refunding of any bonds issued by the Board, and shall also have the
authority to employ attorneys and engineers to facilitate the work of the
Board.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.040)
(Ord. 2017-03, passed 3-6-2017)
§ 31.017 REVENUES.
   The Board may fix and set aside:
   (A)   Revenues of the Department necessary for reasonable and proper
operation and maintenance;
   (B)   Revenues for a proper and adequate Depreciation Account; and
   (C)   Revenues to be applied to the payment of the principal and interest of
the authorized bonds.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.070)
§ 31.018 USE OF REVENUES.
   The revenues set aside to the Depreciation Account shall be expended for:
   (A)   The repair of the storm water system;
   (B)   New acquisitions, construction, extensions or additions to the
property of the storm water system; or
   (C)   Transfer to the Bond and Interest Redemption Account to prevent a
default.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.100)
§ 31.019 DEPRECIATION ACCOUNT AND BOND AND INTEREST REDEMPTION ACCOUNT.
   (A)   In fixing the revenues of the Department required for operation and
maintenance, the Board shall consider the cost of the operation and maintenance
of the Department.
   (B)   If a surplus is accumulated in the Operating and Maintenance Account,
then the Board may transfer any excess over that surplus to:
      (1)   The Depreciation Account, to be used for any improvements,
extensions or additions to the storm water system; or
      (2)   The Bond and Interest Redemption Account.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.080)
§ 31.020 METHODS OF FINANCING.
   The acquisition, construction, installation, operation and maintenance of
the facilities and land for storm water systems may be financed through:
   (A)   The proceeds of special taxing district bonds of the storm water
district;
   (B)   The assumption of liability incurred to construct the storm water
system being acquired;
   (C)   Service rates;
   (D)   Revenue bonds; and
   (E)   Any other available funds.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.050)
§ 31.021 TAXING DISTRICTS.
   A special taxing district of the Department of Storm Water Management shall
include all territory within the corporate boundaries of the city. The
territory within the corporate boundaries of the city shall constitute a
special taxing district for the purpose of providing for the collection and
disposal of the storm water of the district in a manner which protects the
public health and welfare and for the purpose of levying special benefit taxes
for the purpose of storm water collection and disposal.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.030)
§ 31.022 USER FEES.
   The Board, after approval by the Common Council of the city, may assess and
collect user fees from all of the property of the storm water district for the
operation and maintenance of the storm water district.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.060)
§ 31.023 BONDS OF STORM WATER DISTRICT.
   (A)   The bonds of the storm water district are:
      (1)   A valid claim of the holders only against the Bond and Interest
Redemption Account and the revenues of the storm water system; and
      (2)   Exempt from taxation in the state, as provided by I.C. 6-8-5.
   (B)   The bonds may be issued either as registered bonds or as coupon bonds
payable to the bearer.
   (C)   Except as provided in I.C. 5-1-5, bonds shall be sold in accordance
with I.C. 5-1-11. The registration of bonds does not affect negotiability.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.110)
§ 31.024 BOND RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   The Board may not issue any bonds authorized by this subchapter until
it has secured approval for the issuance of the bonds from the legislative body
of the municipality.
   (B)   I.C. 6-1.1-20 applies to the issuance of bonds under this subchapter
which are or may be payable from the special benefit property tax.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.200) (Ord. 1313, passed 9-3-1991)
§ 31.025 MONEY RECEIVED FROM BONDS.
   (A)   All money received from bonds issued under this subchapter shall be
applied solely to the acquisition, construction, repair and maintenance of the
storm water system, the cost of the issuance of the bonds and the creation of
any reserve for the bonds.
   (B)   Any holder of the bonds may bring a civil action to compel the
performance of all duties required by this subchapter of the Board issuing the
bonds or of any officer of the Board, including the following:
      (1)   Making and collecting reasonable and sufficient user fees lawfully
established for services rendered by the storm water system;
      (2)   Segregating the income and revenues of the Department; and
      (3)   Applying the respective funds created under this subchapter.
   (C)   If there is any default in the payment of the principal or interest of
any of the bonds, then a court having jurisdiction of the action may:
      (1)   Appoint an administrator or receiver to administer the storm water
system on behalf of the municipality and the bondholders, with the power to:
         (a)   Charge and collect user fees lawfully established and sufficient
to provide for the payment of the operating expenses and also to pay any bonds
or obligations outstanding against the storm water system;
         (b)   Apply the income and revenues in conformity with this subchapter
and the ordinance; or
         (c)   Declare the whole amount of the bonds due and payable and direct
the sale of the storm water system.
      (2)   Under a sale of the storm water system as ordered in division (C)
(1) above, the purchaser is vested with an indeterminate permit as defined in
I.C. 8-1-2-1 to maintain and operate the storm water system to collect and
dispose of storm water for the municipality and its citizens.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.120)
§ 31.026 PAYMENT OF PRINCIPAL AND INTEREST OF BONDS.
   (A)   The revenues set aside for the payment of the principal and interest
of the authorized bonds shall be deposited and credited to a special account
identified as the Bond and Interest Redemption Account.
   (B)   In determining the amount which is to be set aside for the payment of
the principal and interest of the authorized bonds, the Board may provide that
the amount to be set aside and paid in to the Bond and Interest Redemption
Account for any year or years should not exceed a fixed sum, which must be at
least sufficient to provide for the payment of the interest and principal of
the bonds maturing and becoming payable in each year.
   (C)   If a surplus is created in the Bond and Interest Redemption Account,
then the Board may transfer any excess over the surplus to:
      (1)   The Operation and Maintenance Account; or
      (2)   The Depreciation Account.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.090)
§ 31.027 COSTS AND PAYMENT FOR SERVICES RENDERED BY STORM WATER SYSTEM.
   (A)   The reasonable cost and value of any service rendered to the
municipality by the storm water system by furnishing storm water collection and
disposal shall be:
      (1)   Charged against the municipality; and
      (2)   Paid for in monthly installments as the service accrues out of the:
         (a)   Current revenues of the municipality, whether collected or in
the process of collection; and
         (b)   Tax levy of the municipality made by it to raise money to meet
its necessary current expenses.
   (B)   Compensation for the services provided to the municipality shall, in
the manner prescribed by this subchapter, be treated as revenues of the system
and paid into the funds created under this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.130)
§ 31.028 PROCEDURE FOR IMPROVEMENT PROJECTS.
   (A)   (1)   If, upon investigation, the Board finds that the storm water
system is insufficient to furnish the necessary collection and disposal of
storm water to properly protect the public health and welfare and safeguard the
property within the district, or that it is necessary to acquire, construct,
rebuild, repair, extend or improve the storm water system and equipment, to
acquire lands or to construct, erect or acquire other systems and other
structures and equipment appurtenant to them, then the Board shall prepare
maps, plans, specifications and drawings with full details and descriptions for
the proposed work, together with an estimate of the cost.
      (2)   The Board shall also prepare a description of all property rights
necessary to be acquired in connection with the proposed work and the manner in
which the rights are to be acquired, whether by purchase or appropriation,
along with a description of any other property which may be injuriously
affected, together with the estimated cost.
      (3)   The Board shall then adopt a resolution approving the project by:
         (a)   Declaring that it is necessary for the protection of the public
health and welfare of the inhabitants of the storm water district and the
safeguarding of the property within the district;
         (b)   Declaring that it is of public utility and benefit;
         (c)   Appropriating the property described in the resolution;
         (d)   Stating the maximum proposed cost of any land to be purchased;
and
         (e)   Adopting plans, maps, specifications, drawings, details,
descriptions and estimates.
   (B)   (1)   If the resolution is adopted, then the Board shall publish a
notice in accordance with I.C. 5-3-1 of the adoption of the resolution and of
the fact that plans, specifications and estimates have been prepared and can be
inspected. The notice must also name a date not less than ten days after the
date of the last publication when the Board will receive or hear remonstrances
from the persons interested in, or affected by, the resolution, and when it
will determine the public utility and benefit of the project.
      (2)   Notice shall be mailed to the owners of all property appropriated
by the resolution. If a landowner is a nonresident and the landowner’s place of
residence is known, then a notice shall be mailed to the nonresident owner. If
the nonresident owner’s residence is known to the Board, then the owner is
considered notified of the pendency of the proceedings by the publication of
notice.
   (C)   Separate descriptions of each piece or parcel of land are not required
in the resolution and notice. It is a sufficient description of the property
purchased or to be purchased, or to be appropriated or damaged, to give a
description of the entire tract, whether it is one or more lots or parcels and
whether it is owned by one or more persons. All persons affected by the
proceedings, including all taxpayers in the storm water district, are
considered to be notified of the proceedings and all subsequent acts, hearings,
adjournments and orders of the Board by the original publication of notice.
   (D)   The Board may, before adoption of the resolution, obtain from the
owners of the property an option for its purchase, or the Board may enter into
a contract for its purchase an appraisal by two qualified land appraisers. An
option or contract is subject to the final action of the Board confirming,
modifying or rescinding the resolution.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.140)
§ 31.029 HEARINGS ON PROJECTS; REMONSTRANCES.
   (A)   At the time fixed for the hearing or before the hearing, the following
persons may file a written remonstrance with the Board:
      (1)   The owner of the real property, right- of-way or other property to
be appropriated under the resolution;
      (2)   A person injuriously affected by the appropriation; or
      (3)   A person owning real or personal property within the storm water
district.
   (B)   The Board shall:
      (1)   Hear all persons interested in the proceedings;
      (2)   Hear all of the remonstrances which have been filed; and
      (3)   Take action to confirm, modify or reject the resolution.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.150)
§ 31.030 APPEALS.
   (A)   A person who has remonstrated in writing and is aggrieved by the
decision of the Board may, within 30 days, take an appeal to the Circuit Court
of the county in which the storm water district is located.
   (B)   A remonstrator desiring to appeal the action of the Board shall,
within 30 days after the final action of the Board, file in the office of the
Clerk of the Circuit Court a copy of the order of the Board and the
remonstrance, together with a bond conditioned to pay for the costs of the
appeal should the appeal be determined against the remonstrator.
   (C)   The Court may hear the appeal only if the question is whether the
Board acted arbitrarily or capriciously in adopting the resolution.
   (D)   The cause shall be tried by the Court without a jury.
   (E)   All remonstrances upon which appeals are taken may be consolidated and
heard as one claim for relief by the Court.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.160)
§ 31.031 SPECIAL TAXING DISTRICT BONDS.
   (A)   To procure money to pay for the required property and the acquisition,
erection and construction of the proposed work, and in anticipation of the
collection of the special benefit tax, the Board may issue, in the name of the
municipality, special taxing district bonds of the storm water district. The
bonds may not exceed the total estimated cost of the work and property to be
acquired as provided for in the resolution, including:
      (1)   All expenses necessarily incurred for supervision and inspection
during the period of construction; and
      (2)   Expenses actually incurred preliminary to the acquiring of the
necessary property and the construction of the work, including the costs of
records, engineering expenses, the publication of notices, salaries and other
expenses incurred before and in connection with the acquiring of the property,
the letting of the contract and the sale of bonds.
   (B)   After adopting a resolution authorizing the bonds, the Board shall
certify a copy of the resolution to the municipal Fiscal Officer, who shall
then prepare the bonds. The municipal executive shall execute the bonds and the
Fiscal Officer shall attest the bonds.
   (C)   (1)   The Board may not issue bonds of the storm water district
payable by a special benefit property tax when the total of the outstanding
bonds of the district which are payable from a special benefit property tax,
including the bonds already issued and to be issued, exceeds 8% of the total
assessed valuation of the property within the district after deducting all
exemptions. For the purposes of this section, bonds are not considered to be
outstanding bonds if the payment has been provided for by an irrevocable
deposit in escrow of government obligations sufficient to pay the bonds when
due or called for redemption. The bonds are not a corporate obligation or
indebtedness of the municipality, but are in indebtedness of the storm water
district.
      (2)   The bonds and interest are payable:
         (a)   Out of a special benefit tax levied upon all of the property of
the storm water district; or
         (b)   By any other means, including revenues, cash on hand and cash in
depreciation or reserve accounts.
   (D)   The bonds must recite the terms upon their face, together with the
purpose for which they are issued.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.170)
§ 31.032 SPECIAL BENEFIT TAX.
   (A)   To raise the necessary revenues to pay for the bonds issued and the
interest on said bonds, the Board:
      (1)   After approval by the legislative body of the municipality, shall
levy a special benefit tax upon all of the property of the storm water district
in the amount necessary to meet and pay the principal of the bonds as they
severally mature, together with all accruing interest; and
      (2)   Shall certify the tax levied each year to the Fiscal Officers of
the municipality and of the county in which the storm water district is located
at the same time the levy of the municipality is certified.
   (B)   The tax levied and certified shall be estimated and entered upon the
tax duplicate and shall be collected and enforced in the same manner as state
and county taxes are estimated, entered and enforced. In fixing the amount of
the necessary levy, the Board:
      (1)   Shall consider the amount of revenues derived by the Board from the
operation of the storm water system under its jurisdiction above the amount of
revenues required to pay the costs of the operation and maintenance of the
storm water system; and
      (2)   May, in lieu of making the levy in this section, set aside by
resolution a specific amount of the surplus revenues to be collected before
maturity of the principal and interest of the bonds payable in the following
calender year.
   (C)   The special tax shall be deposited in the Bond and Interest Redemption
Account.
(Prior Code, § 3.80.180)
DEPARTMENT OF PARKS AND RECREATION
§ 31.045 ESTABLISHMENT.
   Under the provisions of I.C. 36-10-3, there is hereby created a municipal
Department of Parks and Recreation.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.010) (Ord. 2015-03, passed 5-4-2015)
§ 31.046 PARKS BOARD; COMPOSITION AND POWERS.
   (A)   Composition. The Parks and Recreation Board shall be composed of six
members who are appointed by the Mayor of the city on the basis of their
interest in and knowledge of parks and recreation. No more than three members
shall be of the same political party.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.020)
   (B)   Powers. The Board shall have the power to perform all acts necessary
to acquire and develop sites and facilities and to conduct such programs as are
generally understood to be parks and recreation functions. In addition, the
Board shall have all of the powers listed in I.C. 36-10-3 et seq.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.050)
(Ord. 2015-03, passed 5-4-2015; Ord. 2021-05, passed 2-1-2021)
§ 31.047 PARKS BOARD; TERM OF OFFICE.
   (A)   Upon the original establishment of the Board, the terms initially
appointed shall be:
      (1)   One member for a term of one year;
      (2)   One member for a term of two years;
      (3)   One member for a term of three years; and
      (4)   One member for a term of four years.
   (B)   In 2021, the city expanded the Parks Board by two members. The terms
of these two new Board members shall be:
      (1)   One member for a term of one year; and
      (2)   One member for a term of two years.
   (C)   As a term expires, each new appointment shall be made by the Mayor for
a term of four years. All terms shall expire on the first Monday in January,
but a member shall continue in office until his or her successor is appointed.
If an appointment for a new term is not made by the executive by the first
Monday in April, then the incumbent shall serve another term. If a vacancy
occurs, then the executive shall appoint a new member for the remainder of the
unexpired term.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.030) (Ord. 2021-05, passed 2-1-2021)
§ 31.048 ELECTING BOARD PRESIDENT AND VICE-PRESIDENT.
   At its first regular meeting each year, the Board shall elect a President
and a Vice-President. The Vice- President shall have the authority to act as
the President of the Board during the absence or disability of the President.
The Board may select a Secretary from within or without its own membership.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.040) (Ord. 2015-03, passed 5-4-2015)
§ 31.049 BUDGET.
   (A)   The Board shall prepare and submit an annual budget in the same manner
as other departments of city government, as prescribed by the State Board of
Accounts.
   (B)   The Board may accept gifts, donations and subsidies for parks and
recreation purposes. However, real estate may only be accepted up by the
approval of the City Board of Public Works and Safety.
(Prior Code, § 2.64.070) (Ord. 2015-03, passed 5-4-2015)
DEPARTMENT OF ECONOMIC DEVELOPMENT
§ 31.060 ESTABLISHMENT.
   There is hereby established a Department of Economic Development, consisting
of the Economic Development Commission organized under I.C. 36-7-12 and having
the powers, duties and responsibilities as set forth therein.
(Prior Code, § 2.04.010) (Ord. 1036, passed 1-5-1984)
YOUTH COUNCIL
§ 31.075 ESTABLISHMENT.
   The City Youth Council is created upon the conditions set forth in this
subchapter. “Youth Council” shall refer to the City Youth Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.010) (Ord. 2004-02, passed 5-3-2004)
§ 31.076 YOUTH COUNCIL MEMBERSHIP; TERM OF OFFICE.
   (A)   Membership.
      (1)   Membership shall be composed of 25 voting members, all between the
grades of five through 11, whom must reside in the territorial limits of the
city and the County Community School Corporation.
      (2)   The Mayor shall appoint one Youth Council Director and the Common
Council shall appoint one Youth Council Director.
      (3)   The Mayor and the Youth Council Directors shall appoint Youth
Council members.
      (4)   The County High School Administration shall be encouraged to
recommend students for appointment to the Youth Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.020)
   (B)   Term of office.
      (1)   Each member of the Youth Council shall be appointed for a term of
two years or until his or her successor is appointed and qualified. A term of
office shall begin on January 1 of each year.
      (2)   Vacancies occurring on the Youth Council after the date of
appointment thereto shall be filled by the Mayor or Youth Council Directors.
The Youth Council may make recommendations to the Mayor or Youth Council
Directors concerning persons to be considered in filling the vacancies.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.030)
(Ord. 2004-02, passed 5-3-2004)
§ 31.077 YOUTH COUNCIL OFFICERS; TERM OF OFFICE.
   (A)   Elected officers. The Youth Council shall elect from its members the
following officers. This election shall take place not later than November 10
of the election year.
      (1)   President. The President shall preside at all meetings of the Youth
Council, correspond with the Mayor and the Common Council at least once each
month and, in addition to the Treasurer, approve all vouchers. The President
shall perform other duties which are normal for a presiding officer.
      (2)   Vice-President. The Vice-President shall preside at all meetings of
the Youth Council during the absence or disability of the President, and shall
perform other duties which the Youth Council shall determine from time to time.
      (3)   Secretary. The Secretary shall attend all meetings of the Youth
Council, take and keep in his or her custody the minutes of all meetings and
provide a copy for the Mayor and the City Clerk-Treasurer. The Secretary shall
perform other duties which the Youth Council shall determine from time to time.
      (4)   Treasurer. The Treasurer shall make a monthly report on the
finances of the Youth Council at the first meeting of each month. He or she
shall also make a written yearly report on all finances of the Youth Council
and provide a copy of this report to the Mayor and Clerk-Treasurer. The
Treasurer, in addition to the President, must approve all vouchers. The
Treasurer shall perform other duties which the Youth Council shall determine
from time to time.
      (5)   Other officers. Other officers or assistants may be elected by the
Youth Council as prescribed in its bylaws.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.040)
   (B)   Term of office. Each officer of the Youth Council shall hold office
for a term of two years and until his or her successor is elected and
qualified.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.050)
(Ord. 2004-02, passed 5-3-2004)
§ 31.078 PURPOSES AND OBJECTIVES.
   The purpose and objectives of the Youth Council are:
   (A)   To provide a direct communication vehicle between the youth of the
city and the city’s administration;
   (B)   To strive for better understanding and communications between the
youth of the city, the city’s administration and the community as a whole;
   (C)   To create its own projects related to Youth Council purposes and
objectives;
   (D)   To encourage the city to provide activities for its young people;
   (E)   To support, aid and assist persons or organizations with ideas or
projects which promote Youth Council purposes and objectives;
   (F)   To provide Youth Council members with the experience of working with
city government; and
   (G)   To provide better understanding and harmonious relationships among
youth.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.070) (Ord. 2004-02, passed 5-3-2004)
§ 31.079 POWERS AND DUTIES.
   (A)   The Youth Council may establish the understanding committees and
special committees, which it determines from time to time.
   (B)   The Youth Council may hold hearings on any matter concerning the
special needs and welfare of those citizens of the city who are under the age
of 18, and it may make written recommendations to the Mayor and to the Common
Council concerning its findings and conclusions from these hearings.
   (C)   The Youth Council may designate one of its members as a liaison person
between the Youth Council and the Common Council of the city.
   (D)   The Youth Council may designate one of its members as a liaison person
between the Youth Council and each of the various boards.
   (E)   (1)   The Youth Council may designate one of its members as a liaison
person between the Youth Council and each of the various boards and commissions
of the city.
      (2)   The Youth Council designee to any board or commission may make
written recommendations concerning that board or commission to the Youth
Council, which may approve, disapprove or modify said recommendations. Approved
recommendations shall be submitted to the Mayor and to the chairperson of the
appropriate board or commission.
   (F)   The Youth Council shall not spend any city monies unless funds are
appropriated by the City Common Council or funds are donated by the public for
the use of the City Youth Council.
   (G)   The Youth Council may adopt written bylaws to govern and regulate its
proceedings. One copy of these bylaws shall be provided to each member of the
Youth Council and one copy shall be provided to the City Clerk-Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.080) (Ord. 2004-02, passed 5-3-2004)
§ 31.080 MEETINGS.
   (A)   The Youth Council shall meet regularly each month. The meeting shall
be held on the same day of each month unless that day is a legal holiday, in
which event the meeting shall be rescheduled for another day which is not a
legal holiday.
   (B)   The day of each regular meeting shall be selected and determined by
the Youth Council at its organizational meeting, and the meeting day may also
be specified in the bylaws of the Youth Council if it adopts a code of bylaws.
   (C)   The Youth Council may meet at other times at special meetings called
by its President or by a majority of the members of the Youth Council.
(Prior Code, § 2.68.060) (Ord. 2004-02, passed 5-3-2004)
CITY COUNCIL FOR THE ARTS
§ 31.095 ESTABLISHMENT; COMPOSITION.
   There shall be established a City Council for the Arts. The Council shall be
composed of five members, one member to be appointed by the Common Council of
the city and four members to be appointed by the Mayor of the city. All members
shall be residents of the city; at the time they cease to be residents of the
city, they shall cease to be members of the Council. Not more than three
members shall be affiliated with the same political party.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.010) (Ord. 1047, passed 5-7-1984)
§ 31.096 TERM.
   The term of membership shall be four years, concurrent with the term of the
Common Council of the city and the Mayor, and shall be appointed upon the
inauguration or commencement of each new city administration.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.020) (Ord. 1047, passed 5-7-1984)
§ 31.097 POWERS.
   The City Council for the Arts shall be empowered to act in a manner to
encourage, maintain and sustain the visual and performing arts within the city
and its immediate vicinity. These powers shall be as outlined in this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.030) (Ord. 1047, passed 5-7-1984)
§ 31.098 ACQUISITION OF LAND, REAL ESTATE OR BUILDINGS.
   The City Council for the Arts shall be empowered, with the approval of the
Common Council of the city, to acquire and maintain any lands, real estate or
buildings necessary for the purpose of encouraging and maintaining the visual
or performing arts. The buildings, lands or real estate shall be used only for
the purposes for which the City Council for the Arts originally acquired them
and shall not revert to any other use without the approval of the Common
Council of the city and, if a grant-in-aid from a foundation or governmental
use was involved in the acquisition, the approval of the foundation or
governmental unit which provided a grant-in-aid for the acquisition.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.040) (Ord. 1047, passed 5-7-1984)
§ 31.099 EMPLOYMENT OF PROFESSIONAL SERVICES.
   (A)   The City Council for the Arts may employ and utilize professional
services for the purpose of encouraging and maintaining the visual and
performing arts in the city limits.
   (B)   The employment of professional services shall take place only when
funds have been appropriated or granted for that specific purpose, and the
employment of professional services shall not exceed in cost the monies
available, appropriated or granted for that specific purpose.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.060) (Ord. 1047, passed 5-7-1984)
§ 31.100 REPORTING OF ACTIVITIES AND FINANCIAL STATUS.
   (A)   The City Council for the Arts shall prepare and furnish to the Common
Council of the city and the Clerk-Treasurer of the city an annual report of its
activities and financial status.
   (B)   The report shall fully and accurately reflect the activities and
financial status of the City Council for the Arts.
(Prior Code, § 2.48.050) (Ord. 1047, passed 5-7-1984)
CITY MUNICIPAL BUILDING CORPORATION
§ 31.115 ESTABLISHMENT.
   It is hereby determined to be proper and in the public interest of the
citizens of the city to reapprove the incorporation of the corporation known
and designated as the City Municipal Building Corporation for the purpose of
financing, improving and equipping municipal facilities and leasing the same to
the city.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.010) (Res. passed 10-18-2004)
§ 31.116 BOARD OF DIRECTORS.
   The Board hereby reapproves the Directors of the City Municipal Building
Corporation.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.070) (Res. passed 10-18-2004)
§ 31.117 ACQUIRING, FINANCING, CONSTRUCTING AND EQUIPPING FACILITIES.
   Providing for the financing, improving and equipping of such municipal
facilities by the City Municipal Building Corporation and the leasing of the
same to the city is in the public interest of the citizens of the city, and it
is a proper public purpose for which the Board agrees to cooperate with the
City Municipal Building Corporation and to assist it in fulfilling the
requirements of all agencies of the federal, state and local governments.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.040) (Res. passed 10-18-2004)
§ 31.118 SALE OF FIRST MORTGAGE BONDS.
   The issuance, sale and delivery by the City Municipal Building Corporation
of bonds designated City Municipal Building Corporation First Mortgage Bonds in
the aggregate principal amount of approximately $1,240,000 is hereby approved.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.050) (Res. passed 10-18-2004)
§ 31.119 REDEMPTION AND RETIREMENT OF BONDS.
   Upon the redemption or retirement of the bonds to be issued by the City
Municipal Building Corporation, the city will accept from the City Municipal
Building Corporation the title to such municipal facilities free and clear of
any and all liens and encumbrances thereon.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.060) (Res. passed 10-18-2004)
§ 31.120 STATUTORY AUTHORITY AND TAX EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   The City Municipal Building Corporation may issue, sell and deliver
its bonds pursuant to the applicable laws of the state, may encumber any real
property or equipment acquired by it for the purpose of financing the
improvements and equipping of such municipal facilities and may enter into
contracts for the sale of the bonds and the improvements to and acquisition of
such municipal facilities.
   (B)   The city reasonably expects that tax-exempt obligations issued by or
on behalf of the city, including First Mortgage Bonds, Series 2005, of the City
Municipal Building Corporation, as well as bonds and temporary loan warrants of
the city, will not exceed $10,000,000 in calendar year 2005. The First Mortgage
Bonds, Series 2005, in the amount of $1,240,000 are designated as qualified
tax-exempt obligations for the purposes of I.R.C. § 265(b) of 1986, being 26
U.S.C. § 265(b).
   (C)   The city reasonably expects that tax-exempt obligations issued by or
on behalf of the city, including the First Mortgage Bonds of the City Municipal
Building Corporation, as well as bonds and temporary loan warrants of the city,
will not exceed $5,000,000 in the calendar year 2005. Pursuant to I.R.C. § 148
(f)(4)(D) of 1986, being 26 U.S.C. § 148(f)(4)(D), as amended, the city
irrevocably allocates to the City Municipal Building Corporation $1,240,000 of
its $5,000,000 limit for the purpose of qualifying for the small governmental
exception to the rebate requirement.
(Prior Code, § 2.60.080) (Res. passed 10-18-2004)
CHAPTER 32: ORDINANCE VIOLATIONS BUREAU
Section
   
32.01   Establishment
   
32.02   Ordinance Violations Clerk duties
   
32.03   Collection of civil penalties for violations
   
32.04   Subsequent and continuing violations
   
32.05   Prosecution procedure for violations
   
32.06   Right to trial
   
32.07   Penalty schedule
§ 32.01 ESTABLISHMENT.
   There is hereby established the Ordinance Violations Bureau of the city.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.010) (Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006)
§ 32.02 ORDINANCE VIOLATIONS CLERK DUTIES.
   (A)   The City Clerk-Treasurer shall serve as the Ordinance Violations Clerk
and be the Administrator of the Bureau.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.020)
   (B)   The Violations Clerk shall accept written appearances, waivers of
trial, admissions of violations and payments of civil penalties of not more
than $250, or in such amount that the General Assembly may hereafter allow in
ordinance violation cases subject to the schedule prescribed under §
32.07 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.030)
(Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006)
§ 32.03 COLLECTION OF CIVIL PENALTIES FOR VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Upon an admission made within 30 days after the date of a citation,
the Clerk shall assess and receive from the violator the amount prescribed by
the schedule of civil penalties established under §
32.07 of this chapter. All citations not admitted and paid within 30 days shall
be transferred to a court of record of competent jurisdiction and prosecuted in
the usual manner.
   (B)   All sums collected by the Violations Clerk as civil penalties for
ordinance violations shall be accounted for and paid to the municipal
corporation as provided by law, I.C. 33-36-3-7 or replacements. Civil penalties
shall be paid to, receipted by and accounted for by the Clerk under procedures
provided for by the State Board of Accounts. The payment of civil penalties
under this chapter may be made in person, by mail or to an agent or agents
designated by the legislative body.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.040) (Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006)
§ 32.04 SUBSEQUENT AND CONTINUING VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Subsequent violations. Any person, corporation or organization which
commits more than one violation of any of the offenses specifically noted
herein within any 12-month period will be subject to an increased fine for each
and every violation as set forth herein.
   (B)   Continuing violations. Every continuous day, or part of a day, in
which a violation is committed or continues in existence is a separate
violation for which civil penalties may be imposed.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.050) (Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006)
§ 32.05 PROSECUTION PROCEDURE FOR VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   If a person does any of the following, then the Clerk shall report
this fact to the official having the responsibility to prosecute ordinance
violation cases for the municipal corporation:
      (1)   Denies an ordinance or code violation under this chapter;
      (2)   Fails to satisfy a civil penalty assessed by the Violations Clerk
after having entered an admission of violation; or
      (3)   Fails to deny or admit the violation under this chapter.
   (B)   Proceedings in court against the person shall then be initiated for
the alleged ordinance violation.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.070) (Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006)
§ 32.06 RIGHT TO TRIAL.
   (A)   A person charged with an ordinance or code violation is entitled to a
trial before a court as provided by law, unless the person waives the right to
trial and enters an admission of the violation with the Violations Clerk.
   (B)   If a person charged with a violation wants to exercise the right to
trial, then the person shall appear before the Violations Clerk and deny the
violation or enter a written denial with the Clerk.
   (C)   Upon denial, the Violations Clerk shall transfer the proceeding to a
court of record located in the county and shall mail a copy thereof to the
person charged. Mailing of the transfer to the last known address of the
charged person as stated in the charge or as furnished by the charged person
shall be deemed notice.
(Prior Code, § 4.04.070) (Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006)
§ 32.07 PENALTY SCHEDULE.
   (A)   The following penalty provisions of this code shall be subject to
admission of violation before the Ordinance Violations Bureau.
