CHAPTER 90: FAIR HOUSING
Section
   
90.01   Policy
   
90.02   Definitions
   
90.03   Equal access to housing in HUD programs
   
90.04   Application
   
90.05   Discrimination in the sale or rental of housing
   
90.06   Discrimination in residential real estate-related transactions
   
90.07   Discrimination in the provision of brokerage services
   
90.08   Interference, coercion or intimidation
   
90.09   Exemptions
   
90.10   Administrative enforcement
 
   
90.99   Penalty
§ 90.01 POLICY.
   It shall be the policy of the city to provide, within constitutional
limitations, for fair housing throughout its corporate limits as provided for
under the federal Civil Rights Act of 1968, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 3601 et seq., as
amended, the federal Housing and Community Development Act of 1974, being 42
U.S.C. §§ 5301 et seq., as amended, and I.C. 22-9.5-1 et seq.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
§ 90.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions apply unless the
context clearly requires a different meaning.
   AGGRIEVED PERSON. Includes any person who:
      (1)   Claims to have been injured by a discriminatory housing practice;
or
      (2)   Believes that such person will be injured by a discriminatory
housing practice about to occur.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-2)
   COMMISSION. The Indiana Civil Rights Commission, created pursuant to I.C.
22-9-1-4 et seq.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-3)
   COMPLAINANT. A person, including the Commission, who files a complaint under
I.C. 22-9.5-6.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-4)
   DISCRIMINATORY HOUSING PRACTICE. An act which is unlawful under §§
90.05 through
90.09 of this chapter or under I.C. 22-9.5-5.
   DWELLING.
      (1)   Any building, structure or part of a building or structure which is
occupied as or designed or intended for occupancy as a residence by one or more
families; or
      (2)   Any vacant land which is offered for sale or lease for the
construction or location of a building, structure or part of a building or
structure which is occupied as or designed or intended for occupancy as a
residence by one or more families.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-8)
   FAMILIAL STATUS.
      (1)   One or more individuals who have not attained the age of 18 years
being domiciled with a parent or another person having legal custody of such
individual or the written permission of such parent or other person.
      (2)   The protections afforded against discrimination on the basis of
FAMILIAL STATUS shall apply to any person who is pregnant or is in the process
of securing legal custody of any individual who has not attained the age of 18
years.
   FAMILY. Includes a single individual (I.C. 22-9.5-2-9), with the status of
such FAMILY being further defined in the definition of familial status.
   HANDICAP.
      (1)   With respect to a person:
         (a)   A physical or mental impairment which substantially limits one
or more of such person’s major life activities;
         (b)   A record of having such an impairment, or being regarded as
having such an impairment;
         (c)   An impairment described or defined pursuant to the federal
Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq.; and
         (d)   Any other impairment defined under 910 I.A.C. 2-3.
      (2)   The term HANDICAP shall not include a current illegal use of or
addictions to a controlled substance as defined in 21 U.S.C. § 802, 910 I.A.C.
2-3-2(14), nor does the term HANDICAP include an individual solely because that
individual is a transvestite, 910 I.A.C. 2-3-2(14).
   PERSON. Includes one or more individuals, corporations, partnerships,
associations, trusts, labor organizations, receivers, legal representatives,
mutual companies, joint-stock companies, unincorporated organizations,
fiduciaries, trustees and trustees in cases under 11 U.S.C.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-11)
   TO RENT. Includes to lease, to sublease, to let and otherwise to grant for
consideration the rights to occupy the premises owned by the occupant.
(I.C. 22-9.5-2-13)
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
§ 90.03 EQUAL ACCESS TO HOUSING IN HUD PROGRAMS.
   Pursuant to 24 C.F.R. § 5.403 and 24 C.F.R. § 574.3, the definition of
FAMILY is revised to include families regardless of the actual or perceived
sexual orientation, gender identity or marital status of its members.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
§ 90.04 APPLICATION.
   Subject to the provisions of division (B) below, §
90.03 of this chapter and I.C. 22-9.5-3, the prohibitions against
discrimination in the sale or rental of housing set forth in I.C. 22-9.5-5-
1 and in §
90.05 of this chapter shall apply to:
   (A)   All dwellings except as exempted by division (B) below and I.C. 22-
9.5-3;
   (B)   Other than the provisions of division (C) below, nothing in §
90.05 shall apply to:
      (1)   Rooms or units in dwellings containing living quarters occupied or
intended to be occupied by not more than four families living independently of
each other if the owner actually maintains and occupies one of such living
quarters as his or her residence; or
      (2)   Any single-family house sold or rented by an owner where the
private individual owner does not own more than three such single-family houses
at any one time, provided that in the sale of such single- family house by a
private individual owner not residing in the house at the time of sale,
exemption shall apply only to one such sale within any 24-month period. The
private individual owner may not own any interest in nor have owned or reserved
on his or her behalf the title to or any right to all or a portion of the
proceeds from the sale or rental of more than three such single-family houses
at any one time. The sale or rental of any such single-family house shall be
exempted from the application of this section only if such house is sold or
rented:
         (a)   Without the use in any manner of the sales or rental facilities
or services of any real estate broker, agent or salesperson, any person in the
business of selling or renting dwellings or any employee or agent of any such
broker, agent, salesperson or person; and
         (b)   Without the publication, posting or mailing, after notice of
advertisement or written notice in violation of §
90.05(A)(3) of this chapter, but nothing in this provision shall prohibit the
use of attorneys, escrow agents, abstracters, title companies and other such
professional assistance as necessary to perfect or transfer said title.
   (C)   For the purpose of division (B) above, a person shall be deemed to be
in the business of selling or renting dwellings if:
      (1)   The person has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as
principal in three or more transactions involving the sale or rental of any
dwelling or any interest therein;
      (2)   The person has, within the preceding 12 months, participated as an
agent in providing sales or rental facilities or services, other than in the
sale of his or her own personal residence, in two or more transactions
involving the sale or rental of any dwelling or any interest therein; or
      (3)   The person is the owner of any dwelling unit designed or intended
for occupancy by, or occupied by, five or more families.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
§ 90.05 DISCRIMINATION IN THE SALE OR RENTAL OF HOUSING.
   (A)   As made applicable by §
90.04 of this chapter and except as exempted by §§
90.03 and
90.04(B) of this chapter, it shall be unlawful:
      (1)   To refuse to sell or rent after the making of a bona fide offer or
to refuse to negotiate for the sale or rental of, or to otherwise make
unavailable or deny, a dwelling to any person because of race, color, religion,
sex, handicap, familial status or national origin;
      (2)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling or in the provision of services or
facilities in connection therewith because of race, color, religion, sex,
handicap, familial status or national origin;
      (3)   To make, print or publish, or to cause to be made, printed or
published, any notice, statement or advertisement with respect to the sale or
rental of a dwelling which indicates any preference, limitation or
discrimination based on race, color, religion, sex, handicap, familial status
or national origin or an intention to make any such preference, limitation or
discrimination;
      (4)   To represent to any person because of his or her race, color,
religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin that any dwelling
is not available for inspection, sale or rental when such dwelling is in fact
so available;
      (5)   For profit, to induce or attempt to induce any person to sell or
rent any dwelling by representations regarding the entry or prospective entry
into the neighborhood of a person or persons of a particular race, color,
religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin;
      (6)   To discriminate in the sale or rental of a dwelling or to otherwise
make unavailable or deny a dwelling to any buyer or renter because of a
handicap of:
         (a)   That buyer or renter;
         (b)   A person residing in or intending to reside in that dwelling
after it is so sold, rented or made available; or
         (c)   Any person associated with that person.
      (7)   To discriminate against any person in the terms, conditions or
privileges of sale or rental of a dwelling or in the provision of services or
facilities in connection with such dwelling because of a handicap of:
         (a)   That person;
         (b)   A person residing in or intending to reside in that dwelling
after it is so sold, rented or made available; or
         (c)   Any person associated with that person.
      (8)   For the purposes of this section, discrimination includes:
         (a)   A refusal to permit, at the expense of the handicapped person,
reasonable modifications of existing premises occupied or to be occupied by
such person if such modifications may be necessary to afford such person full
enjoyment of the premises, except that in the case of a rental, the landlord
may, where it is reasonable to do so, condition permission for a modification
on the renter agreeing to restore the interior of the premises to the condition
that existed before the modifications, reasonable wear and tear excepted;
         (b)   A refusal to make reasonable accommodations in rules, policies,
practices or services when such accommodations may be necessary to afford such
person the equal opportunity to use and enjoy a dwelling; or
         (c)   In connection with the design and construction of covered multi-
family dwellings for first occupancy after the date that is 30 months after
September 13, 1998, a failure to design and construct those dwellings in such a
manner that:
            1.   The public use and common use portions of such dwellings are
readily accessible to and usable by handicapped persons;
            2.   All of the doors designed to allow passage into and within all
premises within such dwellings are sufficiently wide so as to allow for passage
by handicapped persons in wheelchairs; and
            3.   All premises within such dwellings contain the following
features of adaptive design:
               a.   An accessible route into and through the dwelling;
               b.   Light switches, electrical outlets , thermostats and other
environmental controls in accessible locations; and
               c.   Reinforcements in bathrooms such that an individual in a
wheelchair can maneuver about the space.
   (B)   Compliance with the appropriate requirements of the Americans with
Disabilities Act of 1990, being 42 U.S.C. §§ 12101 et seq., and the American
National Standard for Buildings and Facilities providing for accessibility and
usability for physically handicapped people, commonly cited as ANSI A117.1,
suffices to satisfy the requirements of division (A)(8)(c)3.c. above.
   (C)   Nothing in this section requires that a dwelling be made available to
an individual whose tenancy would constitute a direct threat to the health or
safety of other individuals or whose tenancy would result in substantial
physical damage to the property of others.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.06 DISCRIMINATION IN RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED TRANSACTIONS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person or other entity whose business
includes engaging in residential real estate-related transactions to
discriminate against any person because of race, color, religion, sex,
handicap, familial status or national origin in making available such a
transaction or in the terms or conditions of such a transaction.
   (B)   As used in this section, the term RESIDENTIAL REAL ESTATE-RELATED
TRANSACTION means any of the following:
      (1)   The making or purchasing of loans or the providing of other
financial assistance:
         (a)   For purchasing, constructing, improving, repairing or
maintaining a dwelling; or
         (b)   Secured by residential real estate.
      (2)   The selling, brokering or appraising of residential real property.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter prohibits a person engaged in the business of
furnishing appraisals of real property from taking into consideration factors
other than race, color, religion, national origin, sex, handicap or familial
status.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.07 DISCRIMINATION IN THE PROVISION OF BROKERAGE SERVICES.
   It shall be unlawful to deny any person access to, membership in or
participation in any multiple-listing service, real estate brokers’
organization or other service, organization or facility related to the business
of selling and renting dwellings or to discriminate against him or her in the
terms or conditions of such access, membership or participation on account of
race, color, religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.08 INTERFERENCE, COERCION OR INTIMIDATION.
   It shall be unlawful to coerce, intimidate, threaten or interfere with any
person in the exercise or enjoyment of, or on account of his or her having
exercised or enjoyed, or on account of his or her having aided or encouraged
any other person in the exercise or enjoyment of, any right granted or
protected by §§
90.04 through
90.07 of this chapter.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020) Penalty, see §
90.99
§ 90.09 EXEMPTIONS.
   (A)   Exemptions defined or set forth under I.C. 22-9.5-3 et seq. shall be
exempt from the provisions of this chapter, including those activities or
organizations set forth under divisions (B) and (C) below.
   (B)   Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit a religious organization,
association or society, or any nonprofit institution or organization operated,
supervised or controlled by or in conjunction with a religious organization,
association or society, from limiting the sale, rental or occupancy of
dwellings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose to
persons of the same religion or from giving preference to such persons unless
membership in such religion is restricted on account of race, color or national
origin. Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit a private club not in fact open
to the public which, as an incident to its primary purpose or purposes,
provides lodgings which it owns or operates for other than a commercial purpose
from limiting the rental or occupancy of such lodgings to its members or from
giving preference to its members.
   (C)   Nothing in this chapter regarding familial status shall apply with
respect to housing for older persons. As used in this division (C), HOUSING FOR
OLDER PERSONS means housing:
      (1)   Provided under any state or federal program that the Secretary of
the Federal Department of Housing and Urban Development or the State Civil
Rights Commission determines is specifically designed and operated to assist
elderly persons as defined in the state or federal programs;
      (2)   Intended for, and solely occupied by, persons 62 years of age or
older; or
      (3)   Intended and operated for occupancy by at least one person 55 years
of age or older per unit.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
§ 90.10 ADMINISTRATIVE ENFORCEMENT.
   (A)   The authority and responsibility for properly administering this
chapter and the referral of complaints hereunder to the Commission as set forth
in division (B) below shall be vested in the Mayor.
   (B)   Notwithstanding the provisions of I.C. 22-9.5-4-8, because of a lack
of financial and other resources necessary to fully administer enforcement
proceedings and possible civil actions under this chapter, the city herein
elects to refer all formal complaints of a violation of the sections of this
chapter by complainants to the State Civil Rights Commission for administrative
enforcement actions pursuant to I.C. 22-9.5-6, and the Mayor shall refer all
such complaints to the Commission as provided under division (A) above for the
purpose of investigation, resolution and appropriate relief as provided under
I.C. 22-9.5-6.
   (C)   All executive departments and agencies of the city shall administer
their departments, programs and activities related to housing and urban
development in a manner so as to affirmatively further the purposes of this
chapter and shall cooperate with the Mayor and the Commission to further such
purposes.
   (D)   The Mayor or his or her designee shall provide information on
available remedies to any aggrieved person or complainant requesting such
information.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
§ 90.99 PENALTY.
   Whoever, whether or not acting under code of law, by force or threat of
force willfully injures, intimidates or interferes with or attempts to injure,
intimidate or interfere with those listed in divisions (A) through (C) below
shall be fined according to local, state and federal law, and shall be fined
not more than $10,000 or imprisoned not more than ten years, or both, if bodily
injury results, and shall be subject to imprisonment for any term of years or
for life if death results:
   (A)   Any person because of his or her race, color, religion, sex, handicap,
familial status or national origin and because he or she is or has been
selling, purchasing, renting, financing, occupying or contracting or
negotiating for the sale, purchase, rental, financing or occupation of any
dwelling, or has been applying for or participating in any service,
organization or facility related to the business of selling or renting
dwellings;
   (B)   Any citizen, without discrimination on account of race, color,
religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin, because he or she
is or has been participating in, or in order to discourage such citizen or any
other citizen from lawfully aiding or encouraging other persons to participate
in, any of the activities, services, organizations or facilities described in
division (A) above, or because he or she has been participating lawfully in
speech or peaceful assembly opposing any denial of the opportunity to
participate; or
   (C)   Any person because he or she is or has been, or in order to intimidate
such person or any other person or any class of persons from:
      (1)   Participating, without discrimination on account of race, color,
religion, sex, handicap, familial status or national origin, in any of the
activities, services, organizations or facilities described in division (A)
above; or
      (2)   Affording another person or class of persons the opportunity or
protection to so participate.
(Ord. 2020-01, passed 6-1-2020)
CHAPTER 91: PUBLIC MEETINGS, ASSEMBLIES AND CELEBRATIONS
Section
Meetings and Assemblies
   
91.01   Definitions
   
91.02   Public conduct during meetings or assemblies
   
91.03   Duty of property owner or manager
   
91.04   Exemptions
Hartford City Heritage Days
   
91.15   Celebration dates
   
91.16   Parade details
   
91.17   Street closures
   
91.18   Responsible parties
   
91.19   Funding
MEETINGS AND ASSEMBLIES
§ 91.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   ACTIVITY. A public meeting or assembly.
   FUNERAL PROCESSION. A single direct movement of a group of persons from a
mortuary or church to the place of burial of a human body while under the
direction of an authorized funeral director.
   PUBLIC MEETING OR ASSEMBLY. A planned or organized gathering of a group of
persons or any ceremony, show, exhibition or pageant which may reasonably be
expected to result in the gathering of a group of persons upon any public
street, park or other public grounds.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.010)
§ 91.02 PUBLIC CONDUCT DURING MEETINGS OR ASSEMBLIES.
   (A)   Consent needed to assemble. It shall be unlawful for any person to
assemble on a private parking lot or private property without the consent of
the owner or manager of the parking lot or private property.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.040)
   (B)   Prohibited actions.
      (1)   In accordance with the provisions of this subchapter, it is
unlawful for any person to unreasonably obstruct, impede or interfere with any
public meeting or assembly or with any person, vehicle or animal participating
in such a meeting or assembly.
      (2)   Unless by direction of the owner or manager, it shall be unlawful
to intentionally block entrances or exits to any parking area adjacent to any
business building or public building in any manner whereby doing so causes any
difficulty in entering or exiting the premises or adjacent drive or parking
area, except for the purposes of private contractors engaged by the owner or
repairs by municipal authorities.
      (3)   It shall be unlawful for any person to leave an unoccupied motor
vehicle upon a walkway, driveway, parking area or driveway of any business
building or public building without attempting to park the vehicle.
      (4)   It shall be unlawful for any person to leave an unoccupied motor
vehicle upon a walkway, driveway or parking area of any business building or
public building and leave the premises to go elsewhere without the knowledge
and consent of the owner, manager or person in charge of the premises if the
premises is so posted by the owner or manager.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.030)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 91.03 DUTY OF PROPERTY OWNER OR MANAGER.
   It shall be the duty of the owner or manager of a public or business
premises to post notice in a conspicuous location by one or more signs
displaying the fact that the premises is protected by the terms of this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.040)
§ 91.04 EXEMPTIONS.
   This subchapter shall not apply to any of the following:
   (A)   Funeral processions;
   (B)   A governmental agency acting within the scope of its functions; or
   (C)   Students going to and from school classes or participating in
educational activities, provided that the activities are authorized by the
school district and are under the immediate direction and supervision of the
school authorities by the school district to approve and supervise the
activity.
(Prior Code, § 12.04.020)
HARTFORD CITY HERITAGE DAYS
§ 91.15 CELEBRATION DATES.
   The Heritage Days Celebration for calendar year 2018 and all subsequent
years will be held either the second or third weekend in May, consisting of a
Wednesday, Thursday, Friday and Saturday.
(Res. 2019-07, passed 3-4-2019)
§ 91.16 PARADE DETAILS.
   (A)   For the calendar year 2019 and all subsequent years, the Heritage
Parade will be held at 6:00 p.m. on the Wednesday of the Heritage Days
Celebration.
   (B)   The parade will start at the armory on North Jefferson Street and
proceed south, ending at the parking lot at Water Street and Jefferson Street.
   (C)   The City Police Department shall provide escort service for said
parade, and the Street Department will post “no parking” signs along the parade
route for the hours of 4:00 p.m. to 8:00 p.m.
(Res. 2019-07, passed 3-4-2019)
§ 91.17 STREET CLOSURES.
   (A)   The following streets will be closed from 3:00 p.m. on Tuesday until
11:30 a.m. on Sunday:
      (1)   N. High Street between Main Street and Franklin Street;
      (2)   S. High Street at the alley between Washington Street and Water
Street;
      (3)   N. Jefferson Street at the alley between Franklin Street and Main
Street;
      (4)   S. Jefferson Street at the south intersection and east intersection
of Washington Street;
      (5)   W. Main Street at the alley between N. Walnut Street and N. High
Street;
      (6)   E. Main Street at the alley between N. Jefferson Street and N.
Monroe Street; and
      (7)   W. Washington Street at the alley between N. Walnut Street and N.
Jefferson Street.
   (B)   The office of the Mayor will complete and submit a right-of-way permit
from the State Department of Transportation for the closing of State Road 26
from 3:00 p.m. Tuesday until 11:30 a.m. on Sunday.
(Res. 2019-07, passed 3-4-2019)
§ 91.18 RESPONSIBLE PARTIES.
   (A)   The city will provide water service and hook-ups.
   (B)   The city will pay the American Electric Power Company electric bills
for the celebration period upon receipt of a detailed bill.
   (C)   All proper closings and barricades will be the responsibility of the
Street Department.
   (D)   In an effort of spirit and cooperation, the city’s crews will:
      (1)   Fill and deliver sandbags needed for the tents (Street Department);
and
      (2)   Place trash receptacles at appropriate locations throughout the
festival area and empty said receptacles on a daily basis from Thursday through
Sunday at a time determined by the Street Superintendent.
(Res. 2019-07, passed 3-4-2019)
§ 91.19 FUNDING.
   The city hereby commits an annual pledge to the Heritage Days Committee in
the amount of $3,000, to be paid upon a fully-executed claim.
(Res. 2019-07, passed 3-4-2019)
CHAPTER 92: ANIMALS
Section
General Provisions
   
92.01   Animal waste
Dogs and Cats

92.16   Required license and fee
   
92.17   Required immunization
   
92.18   Required sterilization
   
92.19   Protection of dogs and cats
   
92.20   Appropriate shelter, food and water
   
92.21   Actions constituting a nuisance
   
92.22   Dogs and cats at large prohibited
   
92.23   Confining female dogs and cats in heat
   
92.24   Impounding
   
92.25   Kennel dogs
   
92.26   Exemptions
Other Animals
   
92.40   Domestic animals
   
92.41   Rabbits and fowl
   
92.42   Wild animals and vicious animals
   
92.43   Animals at large prohibited
 
   
92.99   Penalty
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 92.01 ANIMAL WASTE.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions apply unless the context clearly requires a different meaning.
      ANIMAL. Any species of bird, mammal, amphibian or reptile.
      GUIDE DOG. Any animal serving a blind person in an auxiliary ocular, or
eye, capacity.
   (B)   Prohibition against animal waste.
      (1)   No person shall knowingly allow an animal to defecate on a public
street, sidewalk, alley or any other right-of-way of the city, on public land,
in public buildings or on private property without the permission of the
landowner.
      (2)   This division (B) shall not apply to guide dogs.
   (C)   Removal of animal waste. If an animal shall defecate, the owner of the
animal is not in violation of this section if that owner immediately removes
any solid waste material and disposes of it in a manner inoffensive to
reasonable public sensibilities. Failure to comply with this division (C) is a
violation.
(Ord. 2016-09, passed 10-3-2016) Penalty, see §
92.99
DOGS AND CATS
§ 92.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   ANIMAL SHELTER. The animal control shelter operated by Blackford County
Animal Shelter, Inc.
   AT LARGE. Any licensed or unlicensed dog or cat found off of the premises of
its owner which is not:
      (1)   Under the control of the owner of the animal, a member of the
owner’s immediate family or a competent person;
      (2)   Retained within a motor vehicle;
      (3)   Housed in a veterinary hospital or kennel;
      (4)   On a leash, cord or chain; or
      (5)   “At heal” beside a competent person and obedient to that person’s
commands.
   CATS. Both male and female animals of the feline species, whether altered or
not.
   DOGS. Both male and female animals of the canine species, whether altered or
not.
   HARBORING. Any person who suffers or permits any dog or cat to frequent or
remain on or within his or her home, building, premises or enclosure shall be
deemed to be HARBORING the animal within the meaning of this subchapter.
   OFFICER. Every law enforcement officer of the County Sheriff’s Department or
City Police Department and employees of Blackford County Animal Shelter, Inc.
   OWNER. Any person or persons, firm, association or corporation owning,
keeping, sheltering or harboring a dog or cat.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017)
§ 92.16 REQUIRED LICENSE AND FEE.
   Every owner of a dog or cat shall pay a fee to and procure a license from
Blackford County Animal Shelter, Inc., at 2520 North 200 East, Hartford City,
Indiana 47348.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.17 REQUIRED IMMUNIZATION.
   (A)   All dogs and cats six months or older shall be vaccinated against
rabies. It shall be a violation of this subchapter for any dog or cat not to be
vaccinated against rabies. A tag showing evidence of proper vaccination shall
be worn by every dog or cat when not confined.
   (B)   Before the issuance of a license, the owner shall furnish a
veterinarian’s certificate showing that the dog or cat for which the license is
sought has been vaccinated, and that the vaccination does not expire within six
months from the effective date of the license.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.18 REQUIRED STERILIZATION.
   (A)   Each dog or cat over the age of six months which is kept in the city
shall have been sterilized and rendered incapable of reproducing by a licensed
veterinarian unless a veterinarian has certified in writing that it would not
be in the animal’s best medical interest.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for a person to own a dog or cat not in
compliance with this section and for which the owner does not have a current
and valid intact breeder’s permit.
   (C)   (1)   A veterinarian who sterilizes a dog or cat shall complete in
triplicate a certificate containing:
         (a)   The owner’s name, address and phone number;
         (b)   The date of sterilization;
         (c)   A description of the animal;
         (d)   The name of the veterinarian’s facility; and
         (e)   The veterinarian’s signature.
      (2)   One copy shall be provided to the owner, one copy to the
veterinarian and one copy to Blackford County Animal Shelter, Inc.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.19 PROTECTION OF DOGS AND CATS.
   It is unlawful for any person to maliciously or mischievously injure or kill
any dog or cat by any means whatsoever.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.20 APPROPRIATE SHELTER, FOOD AND WATER.
   (A)   No person shall confine or allow his or her dog or cat to remain
outside without access to appropriate shelter, which shall be defined as the
following.
      (1)   Doghouses must be weatherproof and have a protected entrance or
wind break or a flexible flap, and must have four sides and a bottom elevated
from the bare ground.
      (2)   Doghouses must contain bedding which resists dampness, such as
straw or cedar chips, during the winter season between November 1 and March 31
or when the real temperature is 45ºF or lower.
      (3)   Kennel areas must be cleaned of feces and debris every 24 hours.
   (B)   All animals shall have fresh, potable water and be provided with food
which is nutritional for the species in adequate amounts so as to maintain good
health.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.21 ACTIONS CONSTITUTING A NUISANCE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for the owner of a dog or cat to allow or permit
the dog or cat to pass upon the premises of another and thereby cause damage
to, or interference with, the premises.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for the owner of a dog or cat to allow or permit
the dog or cat to cause serious annoyance or disturbance to any person or
persons by frequent and habitual howling, yelping, barking or otherwise, or by
running after or chasing persons, bicycles, automobiles or other vehicles.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.22 DOGS AND CATS AT LARGE PROHIBITED.
   No person owning or having charge, care or custody of any dog or cat shall
permit the dog or cat to run at large, whether the dog or cat be licensed or
unlicensed.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.23 CONFINING FEMALE DOGS AND CATS IN HEAT.
   (A)   Every female dog or cat shall be confined in a building or other
secure, humane enclosure while in heat in a manner so that the female dog or
cat cannot come in contact with any male dog or cat except for planned breeding
purposes.
   (B)   While confined, the female dog or cat cannot be readily available for
indiscriminate breeding.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.24 IMPOUNDING.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of every officer to capture each dog and cat
which has been caused, permitted or allowed to be in violation of any of the
provisions of this subchapter and to deliver the dog or cat to Blackford County
Animal Shelter, Inc.
   (B)   Any licensed or unvaccinated dog or cat found at large or any
unlicensed dog or cat found at large in violation of §§
92.22 or
92.23 of this chapter shall be seized and impounded by Blackford County Animal
Shelter, Inc.
   (C)   The owner of a licensed dog or cat shall be notified within two days
that upon payment of the impounding fee, plus the cost of food and care in a
reasonable amount, the dog or cat will be returned. If an impounded licensed
dog or cat is not recovered by its owner within five days after notice, the dog
or cat may be put up for adoption.
   (D)   Upon proper identification, an impounded unlicensed dog or cat may be
recovered by the owner by payment of the license fee, impounding fee and
boarding costs, as well as the cost of vaccination if vaccination is required
by §
92.17 of this chapter. If the dog or cat is not claimed within five days after
notice, it may be put up for adoption.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017)
§ 92.25 KENNEL DOGS.
   Kennel dogs kept or raised solely for the bona fide purpose of sale and kept
under constant restraint are subject to the provisions of this subchapter.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017)
§ 92.26 EXEMPTIONS.
   The provisions of this subchapter shall not apply:
   (A)   To dogs brought into the city for the purpose of participating in any
dog show; or
   (B)   To “seeing eye” or guide dogs properly trained to assist blind persons
when the dogs are actually used by blind persons for the purpose of aiding them
in going from place to place.
(Ord. 2017-10, passed 12-4-2017)
OTHER ANIMALS
§ 92.40 DOMESTIC ANIMALS.
   (A)   Within the limits of the city, no person shall keep or permit to be
kept on his or her premises any horse, mare, colt, mule, jackass, jenny, burro,
pony, bull, ox, calf, goat, sheep, hog, pig, llama, alpaca or any other hoofed
animal unless such person shall have been engaged in a farming operation
involving these animals on such premises prior to the passage of this
subchapter.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to any animal brought into the city for a
circus, parade or animal show or exhibition.
(Prior Code, § 6.06.010) (Ord. 1029, passed 7-5-1983; Ord. 2013-16, passed 10-
7-2013) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.41 RABBITS AND FOWL.
   (A)   All rabbits and fowl within the city limits shall be completely
confined in an enclosure of adequate size which has sides, one or more doors, a
roof and a floor, and shall be kept in the enclosure at all times.
   (B)   No rabbit or fowl shall be permitted to run in an enclosure at all
times. No rabbit or fowl shall be permitted to run in an enclosure pen even
though the pen may be connected to a proper enclosure as provided in division
(A) above.
(Prior Code, § 6.06.010) (Ord. 1029, passed 7-5-1983) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.42 WILD ANIMALS AND VICIOUS ANIMALS.
   (A)   No person shall keep or permit to be kept on his or her premises any
wild animal or other animal known to be vicious.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to any animal brought into the city for a
period of less than seven days for the purpose of a circus, parade or animal
show or exhibition.
(Prior Code, § 6.06.010) (Ord. 1029, passed 7-5-1983) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.43 ANIMALS AT LARGE PROHIBITED.
   (A)   Public property. No person who keeps, owns or harbors any animal
referred to in this subchapter shall cause, permit or allow the same to be at
large or run at large upon any street, alley or other public place within the
city limits.
   (B)   Private property. No person who keeps, owns or harbors any animal
referred to in this subchapter shall cause, permit or allow the same to be at
large or run at large upon any private property or premises within the city
limits.
(Prior Code, § 6.06.020) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   General penalty. Any person violating any provision of this chapter
for which no specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Animal waste. Any person who violates the provisions of §
92.01 of this chapter shall pay a fine as follows:
      (1)   First offense: $25;
      (2)   Second offense: $50; and
      (3)   Subsequent offenses: $100.
   (C)   Dogs and cats.
      (1)   Any person violating any provision of §§
92.16,
92.17 or
92.20 through
92.23 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be subject to a fine not
exceeding $20 for the first offense, $50 for the second offense or $100 for the
third or subsequent offenses, provided that the city must allege and prove the
dates and case numbers of the previous convictions. If the dog or cat was not
wearing a current tag attached thereto, the person shall be fined in an amount
double the fine set forth in this division (C)(1).
      (2)   Any owner violating any of the provisions of §
92.23 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be subject to a fine not
exceeding $100.
      (3)   A violation of §
92.18 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine not less than $100.
   (D)   Other animals. Any person who violates any provision of §§
92.40 through
92.43 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than $5 and not
more than $50, plus court costs. Each day shall constitute a separate violation
of §§
92.40 through
92.43 of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 6.06.030)
(Ord. 1029, passed 7-5-1983; Ord. 2016-09, passed 10-3-2016; Ord. 2017-10,
passed 12-4-2017)
CHAPTER 93: NUISANCES
Section
General Provisions
   
93.01   Nuisances prohibited
   
93.02   Abatement notices
   
93.03   Hearings
   
93.04   Failure to abate and collection of costs
Noise
   
93.15   Prohibited noise
   
93.16   Respecting quiet zones
   
93.17   Disposition of fines
   
93.18   Permits
   
93.19   Exemptions
 
   
93.99   Penalty
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 93.01 NUISANCES PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person shall erect, construct, cause, permit, keep or maintain
within the city limits anything whatsoever which is injurious to the public
health or safety or which is offensive to the senses of inhabitants. The
existence of any of the above is declared to be a nuisance and shall be
regulated as set forth in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.010)
   (B)   The following are declared to be nuisances, but shall not be construed
as preventing any other thing from being declared a nuisance pursuant to the
standards of division (A) above:
      (1)   Erecting or using any building or other place for the exercise of
any trade, employment or manufacture which, by occasioning dense smoke or ash,
noxious exhalations or other annoyances, becomes harmful to the health, safety
or property of individuals or the public;
      (2)   Causing or suffering any offal, filth or waste to be collected or
to remain in any place to the prejudice of others;
      (3)   Obstructing or encumbering, by any means whatsoever, the private
ways or the public streets, alleys and places so as to create a physical threat
to the public; and
      (4)   Billboards, signboards and advertising signs, whether erected and
constructed on public or private property, or overhanging branches or
vegetation obstructing or impairing the view of any portion of a pubic street
or alley of the city so as to render dangerous the use thereof.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.020)
Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.02 ABATEMENT NOTICES.
   (A)   Issuance of notice. Whenever the Police Chief finds that a nuisance
exists, he or she shall cause to be served upon the property owner, as shown by
the records of the County Auditor, a written notice to abate the nuisance
within a reasonable time after the notice. The notice shall be sent to the
property owner by certified mail.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.030)
   (B)   Contents of notice. The notice to abate shall contain:
      (1)   A description of what constitutes the nuisance;
      (2)   The location of the nuisance;
      (3)   A statement of the act or acts necessary to abate the nuisance;
      (4)   A reasonable time within which to complete the abatement; and
      (5)   A statement that if the nuisance is not abated as directed and no
request for hearing is made within the time prescribed, then the city will
abate said nuisance and assess the cost against the property owner.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.040)
Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.03 HEARINGS.
   (A)   Any person ordered to abate a nuisance may have a hearing with the
officer ordering the abatement to determine whether a nuisance does exist. A
request for a hearing must be made in writing and delivered to the officer
ordering the abatement within the time stated in the notice or else it will be
conclusively presumed that a nuisance exists that must be abated as ordered.
   (B)   (1)   At the conclusion of the hearing, the Hearing Officer shall
render a written decision as to whether a nuisance exits. If he or she finds
that a nuisance exists, then he or she must order it abated within an
additional time which is reasonable under the circumstances.
      (2)   An appeal from this decision may be made by immediately filing
written notice with the Hearing Officer. This appeal will be heard before the
Common Council at a time and place fixed by the Common Council. The findings of
the Common Council shall be ordered abated within a time reasonable under the
circumstances.
   (C)   The Director of Redevelopment and Environmental Affairs shall perform
the duties of Hearing Judge as required under this section and chapter, and
shall fulfill all responsibilities accruing to the position of Hearing Judge as
herein provided.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.050) (Ord. 2000-1, passed 5-1-2000)
§ 93.04 FAILURE TO ABATE AND COLLECTION OF COSTS.
   (A)   If a person notified to abate a nuisance neglects or fails to abate as
directed, then the city may perform the action or actions required to abate
said nuisance, keeping an accurate account of expenses incurred. An itemized
expense account shall be certified and filed with the Clerk-Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.060)
   (B)   The Clerk-Treasurer shall send by certified mail a statement of the
total expenses incurred to the property owner who has failed to abide by the
notice to abate, and if the amount shown by the statement has not been paid
within one month, then the Clerk- Treasurer shall certify the costs to the
County Auditor. The amount due shall then be collected with, and in the same
manner as, general property taxes and disbursed into the General Fund of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.070)
Penalty, see §
93.99
NOISE
§ 93.15 PROHIBITED NOISE.
   (A)   It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to create or assist
in creating any unreasonably loud and disturbing noise in the city. Noise of a
character, intensity and duration so as to be detrimental to the public health,
welfare and peace is prohibited.
   (B)   Loud and disturbing noises are declared to be, but are not exclusive
to, the following:
      (1)   The sounding of any horn or signal device in any automobile,
motorcycle, bus or other vehicle, except as a danger signal, so as to create
any unreasonably loud or harsh sound, or the sounding of such device for an
unreasonable period of time, or the use of any gong or siren upon any vehicle
other than a police, fire or other emergency vehicle;
      (2)   The playing of any radio, phonograph or other musical instrument in
a manner or with a volume so as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or
repose of any person in any dwelling, hotel or other type of residence,
particularly during the hours between 11:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m.;
      (3)   The keeping of any animal or bird which shall disturb the comfort
and repose of any person in the vicinity by causing frequent or long, continued
noises;
      (4)   The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair,
so loaded or in such a manner so as to create loud grating, grinding, rattling
or other noises;
      (5)   The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler
or engine, except to give notice of the time to begin or stop work or as a
warning of danger;
      (6)   The sounding of any bell or gong attached to any building or
premises which disturbs the quiet and repose of persons in the vicinity
thereof;
      (7)   The conducting, operating or maintaining of any garage or service
station in any residential area so as to cause loud and offensive noises to be
emitted therefrom between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. on weekdays or
on Sundays;
      (8)   The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to a
school, institution of learning or court while the same are in session, or
within 150 feet of any hospital, which unreasonably interferes with the working
of those institutions, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed in those
streets indicating the area is a school, court or hospital area;
      (9)   The creation of any excessive noise on Sundays on any street
adjacent to any church, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed in the
streets adjacent to churches indicating that the same is a church street;
      (10)   The erection, including excavation, or demolition, alteration or
repair of any building in a residential or business district other than between
the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. on weekdays, except for in cases of urgent
necessity in the interest of public safety, and then only with a permit from
the Building Inspector, which permit may be renewed for a period of three days
or less while said emergency continues;
      (11)   The use of any mechanical device operated by compressed air unless
the noise created thereby is muffled and reduced;
      (12)   The shouting and crying of peddlers, barkers, hawkers and venders
which disturbs the quiet and peace of the neighborhood;
      (13)   The use of any drum, loudspeaker or other instrument or device for
the purpose of attracting attention to any performance, show or display or sale
of merchandise by the creation of noise; or
      (14)   The use of any mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks or
other moving vehicles for advertising or other purposes, except where specific
license is received from the Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.090) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.16 RESPECTING QUIET ZONES.
   Within any quiet zone established by the Board of Public Works and Safety of
the city, no person shall make, cause to be made, permit or suffer to be made
any loud, unusual or unnecessary noises, nor disturb or otherwise annoy the
inhabitants of the quiet zone, and especially the occupants and patients of any
hospital, with loud, unusual or unnecessary noise, disorder or tumult of any
kind.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.090) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.17 DISPOSITION OF FINES.
   All fines collected upon the conviction of any person charged with a
violation of any of the provisions established in §§
93.15 and
93.16 of this chapter shall be deposited in the City General Fund.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.090)
§ 93.18 PERMITS.
   (A)   The Police Department of the city may issue guidelines defining the
procedures to be followed in applying for a permit and the specific criteria to
be considered in deciding to issue a permit. Permits may contain any conditions
necessary to limit the adverse impact of the activity, including a time limit.
   (B)   The Police Department of the city shall have the authority to issue
permits for:
      (1)   Holidays, celebrations, concerts, parades, school and athletic
events, special park and recreational activities or other special events, both
public or personal; and
      (2)   Persons who demonstrate that bringing the source of sound or
activity for which a permit is sought into compliance with the provisions of
this subchapter would constitute a hardship on the applicant, the community or
other persons, and that the adverse impact on the health, safety and welfare of
the persons affected by the permit has been outweighed by the hardship.
   (C)   Noncompliance with any condition of a permit issued shall terminate
the permit and subject the person or persons holding the permit to the
provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.090) Penalty, see §
93.99
§ 93.19 EXEMPTIONS.
   The provisions of this subchapter pertaining to restrictions on noise
emission and the emission of sounds shall not apply when the noise or sound
emission is for the purpose of alerting persons to the existence of an
emergency nor to the emission of sound in the performance of work to prevent or
alleviate physical or property damage threatened or caused by a public calamity
or other emergency.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.090)
§ 93.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   General penalty. Any person violating any provision of this chapter
for which no specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Nuisances.
      (1)   In addition to the collection of costs as defined in §
93.04 of this chapter, any property owner or owners failing to abate nuisances
under the provisions of §§
93.01 through
93.04 of this chapter shall be assessed a penalty of $100 per count of
violation of §§
93.01 through
93.04 of this chapter.
      (2)   Each and every day or portion thereof which elapses after the final
order to abate the nuisance under the procedures defined in §§
93.01 through
93.04 of this chapter shall be deemed to constitute a single and individual
count of violation and shall be assessed the fine for each violation so
defined.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.080)
   (C)   Noise.
      (1)   Any person found in violation of the motor vehicle noise limits set
forth in §
93.15 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $50 nor more than $200.
      (2)   Any person found in violation of any other provision of §§
93.15 through
93.19 of this chapter shall be fined not less than $25 for a first offense, not
less than $75 for a second offense and not less than $150 for a third and
subsequent offenses.
      (3)   Each day that a violation is in effect shall constitute a separate
offense.
(Prior Code, § 8.04.090)
(Ord. 2002-16, passed 11-4-2002; Ord. 2003-04, passed 7-7-2003)
CHAPTER 94: HEALTH AND SAFETY
Section

WEED CONTROL
§ 94.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition applies unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   WEEDS AND RANK VEGETATION.
      (1)   Grass, weeds, volunteer plants, shrubs, bushes or other vegetation
growth which is not planted or cultivated, excepting trees, flowers, garden
vegetables and agricultural crops such as hay and pasture, and which exceed six
inches in height.
      (2)   In addition to the foregoing, any and all dead and diseased flora
which meets the description set forth in §
157.43 of this code, even if the same be trees, flowers, garden vegetables or
agricultural crops, may be considered WEEDS AND RANK VEGETATION for the purpose
of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.010) (Ord. 2005-07, passed 6-6-2005; Ord. 2009-11, passed
8-3-2009)
§ 94.02 UNLAWFUL GROWTH PROHIBITED.
   The owner of any lot or parcel of land within the city shall not allow the
grass, lawn, weeds or vegetation growing on the lot or parcel of land to exceed
six inches in length.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.010) (Ord. 2005-07, passed 6-6-2005; Ord. 2009-11, passed
8-3-2009) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.03 NOTICE TO REMOVE.
   (A)   Pursuant to I.C. 36-7-10.1-3, the Common Council shall require the
owners of real property in the city to cut and remove weeds and other rank
vegetation in excess of six inches in length growing on that property.
   (B)   The adoption and publication of this subchapter shall constitute
notice to each property owner.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.020) (Ord. 2005-07, passed 6-6-2005)
§ 94.04 REMOVAL COSTS CHARGED.
   (A)   If a landowner fails to remove vegetation as described herein, then
the city shall remove the vegetation. The Clerk-Treasurer shall make a
certified endorsement of the costs incurred by the city in the removal. The
statement shall be delivered to the owner of the property by mail, postage
prepaid, at the mailing address maintained by the County Treasurer for real
estate tax correspondence.
   (B)   Simultaneously with division (A) above, the Clerk-Treasurer shall file
a certified copy of the statement of costs in the office of the Auditor of the
county in which the property is located. The Auditor shall place the amount
claimed on a tax duplicate against the property affected by the work, and the
amount shall be collected as taxes are collected and shall be disbursed to the
General Fund of the city.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.030) (Ord. 655, passed 6-1-1964; Ord. 2005-07, passed 6-6-
2005) Penalty, see §
94.99
ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES
§ 94.15 PURPOSE.
   The Common Council, recognizing the existence of abandoned and junk vehicles
and vehicles constituting a nuisance in the yards of residences within the
city, in open lots and encroaching upon the rights-of-way of streets, alleys
and highways within the city, and being desirous to obtain and enforce the
removal of such vehicles in order to protect the general welfare of the city
and its citizens, does hereby and herewith declare such abandoned and junk
vehicles to be a nuisance.
(Ord. 2016-07, passed 8-1-2016)
§ 94.16 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   ABANDONED AND JUNK VEHICLES. Any one of the following:
      (1)   A vehicle illegally located on public property;
      (2)   A vehicle left on public property without being moved for three
days;
      (3)   A vehicle located on public property in such a manner so as to
constitute a hazard or an obstruction to the movement of pedestrian or
vehicular traffic on a public right-of-way;
      (4)   A vehicle which has remained on private property without the
consent of the owner or person in control of said property for more than 48
hours;
      (5)   A vehicle from which the engine, transmission or differential has
been removed or which is otherwise partially dismantled or inoperable and left
on public property;
      (6)   A vehicle which has been removed by a towing service or public
agency upon the request of an officer enforcing a statue or ordinance other
than this subchapter if the vehicle removed is not claimed or redeemed by the
owner or the owner’s agent within 15 business days of the vehicle’s removal; or
      (7)   A vehicle which is in a mechanically- inoperable condition or with
no current registration and left on private property continuously in a location
which is visible from public property for more than ten days.
   INOPERABLE CONDITION. All types of motor-driven vehicles used or usable for
the conveyance of persons or property which are unable to move under their own
power due to defective or missing parts, and which have remained in such
condition for a continuous period of not less than ten consecutive days. Such a
motor vehicle shall also include all types of motor-driven vehicles which,
although able to move under their own power, are in such a condition due to
defective or missing parts so as to be dangerous or unfit for further use as a
conveyance upon the public highways.
   NUISANCE. Because of the danger to health from vermin and insects and to
children attracted by the same, motor vehicles in an inoperative condition and
motor vehicles unfit for further use which are situated within the corporate
limits of the city and which are not inside a garage or other building are
hereby declared and defined to be a NUISANCE, except when such motor vehicle is
within a lawfully operated junk yard or a yard lawfully operated for the
storage of vehicles awaiting permission for junking from the State Bureau of
Motor Vehicles.
(Ord. 2016-07, passed 8-1-2016)
§ 94.17 ENFORCEMENT AUTHORITY.
   Any member of the City Police Department is designated to enforce this
subchapter within the city.
(Ord. 2016-07, passed 8-1-2016)
§ 94.18 WRITTEN NOTICE TO REMOVE.
   Written notice giving five days to remove such motor vehicle shall be placed
upon the motor vehicle to be removed. When convenient, copies of said written
notice shall be served upon any adult occupying the real estate upon which such
motor vehicle is located or upon the record owner of such motor vehicle.
(Ord. 2016-07, passed 8-1-2016) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.19 FEES AND EXPENSES CHARGED.
   The city may charge any expenses incurred by it in the enforcement of this
subchapter, including all towing and storage charges, to the owner or occupant
of the real estate upon which that vehicle is located or to the owner of the
motor vehicle.
(Ord. 2016-07, passed 8-1-2016) Penalty, see §
94.99
OPEN STORAGE OF HAZARDOUS MATERIALS
§ 94.30 UNSAFE OPEN STORAGE PROHIBITED.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person owning or having possession and
control of real estate within the corporate limits of the city to permit the
open storage of materials in a hazardous or unhealthful manner as set out in
this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.010)
   (B)   This subchapter shall apply to the open storage of materials which
consist of materials not stored in a permanent enclosure, warehouse, garage or
fenced area. A fenced area or enclosed area must be sufficiently restrictive so
as to prevent the materials contained from being offensive or from presenting
an unreasonable health or safety hazard to the community.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.020)
Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.31 TYPES OF MATERIALS.
   Types of materials:
   (A)   Wood materials such as lumber, firewood or paper products;
   (B)   Stone or masonry materials such as bricks, concrete blocks, sand or
gravel;
   (C)   Glass materials such as bottles or plate glass;
   (D)   Metal materials such as scrap steel iron or used metal products; and
   (E)   Rubber materials such as used tires.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.020)
§ 94.32 STORAGE RESTRICTIONS.
   The following restrictions are set out pursuant to maintaining materials set
forth in §
94.31 of this chapter.
   (A)   The open storage of materials shall not be offensive to persons of
ordinary sensibility. The materials stored shall not present a substantial
visual detraction to the community. The materials shall not produce obnoxious
odors. Handling or processing the materials shall not produce excessive noise
discomfort.
   (B)   Materials shall be stored in a manner reasonably calculated to
minimize the danger of physical injury to the general public or passers-by.
      (1)   Materials must be placed a distance of at least ten feet from the
surface of any street, alley, sidewalk or passage, thereby reducing the
attraction to children, minimizing vehicle line-of-sight obstructions and
allowing for the safe passage of pedestrians and motorists.
      (2)   Materials must be stacked in a mechanically-sound manner so as to
prevent the materials from shifting or falling. The stack height shall be
limited to two times the lesser of the width or length of the stack.
   (C)   Care in the placement and maintenance of stored materials shall be
exercised to reduce potential fire hazards. Flammable materials in the nature
of wood or rubber materials shall not be stored within ten feet of any dwelling
house. Open storage of any highly flammable or combustible materials is not
permitted.
   (D)   The open storage of the materials described in this subchapter shall
not be permitted to become a health hazard. The materials stored or maintained
shall not present an unreasonable attraction to rodents, birds or other pests.
Decaying, insect-infested or otherwise unsanitary materials are not permitted
to be stored or collected.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.030) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.33 NOTICE TO ABATE.
   Any person who shall violate the restrictions set forth in this subchapter
will be given notice by the City Police Department. The person shall have ten
days to correct the condition, beginning from the date of receiving official
notice of a violation of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.040) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   General penalty. Any person violating any provision of this chapter
for which no specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Weed control.
      (1)   In addition to the collection of costs assessed in §
94.04 of this chapter, any landowner or owners failing to remove vegetation
under the provisions of §§
94.01 through
94.04 of this chapter within the ten days allowed for removal after
notification under the terms of §§
94.01 through
94.04 of this chapter shall be assessed a penalty of $50 per count of violation
defined in §§
94.01 through
94.04 of this chapter.
      (2)   Each and every day, or portion thereof, that elapses after the ten
days allowed to remove the vegetation under the procedures defined in §§
94.01 through
94.04 of this chapter shall be deemed to constitute a single and individual
count of violation and shall be assessed the penalty herein established for
each violation so defined.
(Prior Code, § 8.24.040)
   (C)   Abandoned and junk vehicles.
      (1)   Any person who fails to comply with any order to remove an
abandoned or junk vehicle issued under §§
94.15 through
94.19 of this chapter shall be deemed to have committed an ordinance violation,
and upon conviction, the owner of the abandoned or junk vehicle, the occupant
of the real estate upon which that vehicle is located or the owner of that real
estate shall be fined $50 for the first offense and $100 for each subsequent
offense within one year, plus the court costs of the enforcement of §§
94.15 through
94.19 of this chapter, including towing, storage fees and disposal costs.
      (2)   Each day that a violation occurs or continues after the expiration
date of the order to remove such vehicle shall constitute a separate offense.
   (D)   Hazardous materials.
      (1)   If a person continues to violate the provisions of §§
94.30 through
94.33 of this chapter after being given proper notice to abate as set forth in
§
94.33 of this chapter, then such person shall be assessed a civil penalty as
set forth in §
32.07 of this code, and each day such violation continues shall be deemed a
separate offense.
      (2)   Any person, firm or corporation who shall continue to violate any
of the provisions of §§
94.30 through
94.33 of this chapter beyond the time limit provided for in the written notice
of the violation shall be assessed a civil penalty as set forth in §
32.07 of this code for each violation. Each day in which any violation may
continue shall be deemed a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 8.12.050)
(Ord. 970, passed 8-15-1977; Ord. 2002-17, passed 11-4-2002; Ord. 2006-02,
passed 6-5-2006; Ord. 2016-07, passed 8-1-2016)
CHAPTER 95: FIRE PREVENTION AND PROTECTION
Section
Open Burning
   
95.01   Definitions
   
95.02   Refuse burning prohibited
   
95.03   Trade waste burning restrictions
   
95.04   Agricultural waste burning restrictions
   
95.05   Tree leaf burning restrictions
Fireworks
   
95.20   Location restrictions
   
95.21   Date and time restrictions
 
   
95.99   Penalty
OPEN BURNING
§ 95.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   AGRICULTURAL WASTE. The byproducts of waste materials from any type of
agricultural operation.
   REFUSE. Any type of filth, vegetable matter, straw, paper, food, wood,
glassware, garbage, rubbish, sweepings of any kind or any type of material
which is being disposed of as waste.
   TRADE WASTE. The waste products from any manufacturing operation or any
business operation.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.010)
§ 95.02 REFUSE BURNING PROHIBITED.
   It shall be a violation of this subchapter for any person to cause, suffer
or allow refuse to be burned within the city limits.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.020) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.03 TRADE WASTE BURNING RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   No person shall permit the disposal of trade waste by open burning,
except that the open burning of trade waste may be permitted when it can be
shown that open burning is necessary and in the public interest.
   (B)   Any person intending to initiate the open burning of trade waste shall
file an application to do so with the Mayor. The application shall state the
following:
      (1)   The name, address and telephone number of the person submitting the
application;
      (2)   The type, purpose or activity involved;
      (3)   A description of the equipment and operating practices and of the
type, quality and composition of the trade waste to be permitted;
      (4)   The schedule of burning operations;
      (5)   The exact location where open burning will be used to dispose of
trade waste; and
      (6)   The reasons why no method other than burning can be used for the
disposal of trade wastes.
   (C)   (1)   The Mayor shall have the authority to approve any application
for the open burning of trade waste and shall do so in writing.
      (2)   His or her approval shall be on file in the office of the Clerk-
Treasurer in the city.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.030) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.04 AGRICULTURAL WASTE BURNING RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   The open burning of agricultural waste shall be permitted only between
the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 4:00 p.m., and only at times when the actual
forecast of wind, when given by the local Weather Bureau, is five mph or less.
   (B)   The open burning of agricultural waste shall be done only when
necessary and when no fire hazard will occur.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.040) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.05 TREE LEAF BURNING RESTRICTIONS.
   The burning of tree leaves in a manner that shall cause nuisance, detriment
or annoyance to any person of the public is prohibited, except between the
hours of 10:00 a.m. to one hour before sundown when no fire hazard will occur.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.050) Penalty, see §
95.99
FIREWORKS
§ 95.20 LOCATION RESTRICTIONS.
   No person within the limits of the city may ignite, discharge or use
fireworks at a site other than:
   (A)   The property of the person; or
   (B)   The property of another person who has given permission to use
fireworks on his or her property.
(Ord. 2018-12, passed 11-5-2018) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.21 DATE AND TIME RESTRICTIONS.
   Fireworks may not be used, ignited or discharged within the limits of the
city on dates and at times other than as follows:
   (A)   Between the hours of 5:00 p.m. and 11:00 p.m. on June 29, June 30,
July 1, July 2, July 3, July 5, July 6, July 7, July 8 and July 9;
   (B)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m., midnight, on July 4;
or
   (C)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. on December 31 and 1:00 a.m. on
January 1.
(Ord. 2018-12, passed 11-5-2018) Penalty, see §
95.99
§ 95.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   General penalty. Any person violating any provision of this chapter
for which no specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Open burning.
      (1)   Any person violating any of the provisions of §§
95.01 through
95.05 of this chapter shall be assessed a civil penalty as set forth in §
32.07 of this code. Each and every violation of the provisions of §§
95.01 through
95.05 of this chapter shall constitute a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.060)
      (2)   Any person found violating the provisions of §
95.05 of this chapter and found guilty shall be punished by a fine as follows:
         (a)   First violation: $10; and
         (b)   Each subsequent violation: $25.
(Prior Code, § 8.08.050)
   (C)   Fireworks. Any person or persons violating any of the provisions of §§
95.20 or
95.21 of this chapter shall, upon conviction, be subject to a fine not
exceeding $20 for a first offense, $50 for a second offense and $100 for a
third and subsequent offences.
(Ord. 968, passed 10-3-1977; Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006; Ord. 2018-12,
passed 11-5-2018)

CITY PARKS AND POOLS
§ 96.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions apply unless
the context clearly requires a different meaning.
   BOARD. The Board of Parks and Recreation of the city.
   PARK. Any land owned or controlled by the Board of Parks and Recreation of
the city.
   PERSON. Includes persons and corporations.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.150)
§ 96.02 HOURS OF OPERATION.
   All parks will open at 7:00 a.m. and close at 9:00 p.m., with the exception
of parks which have a designated athletic field, swimming pool or court
lighting, where said parks will open at 7:00 a.m. and close at 11:00 p.m. The
basketball court at Sigma Phi Gamma park shall close at 9:00 p.m. Hours may be
extended by permission of the Board.
(Ord. 2012-10, passed 4-2-2012)
§ 96.03 PRESERVATION OF PROPERTY AND NATURAL FEATURES.
   No person shall injure, deface or disturb any part of a park or any
building, sign or equipment, nor may other property or minerals be removed,
injured or destroyed.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.030) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.04 HUNTING AND MOLESTING WILDLIFE.
   (A)   No person shall hunt, pursue with dogs, trap or in any other way
molest any wild bird or animal found within the confines of the parks, nor
therein rob or molest any bird nest or take the eggs of any bird.
   (B)   A person may fish from park property if he or she follows the fishing
regulations as stated by the State Department of Natural Resources.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.040) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.05 CAMPING.
   No person shall establish or maintain any camp or other temporary lodging
place on park property without a permit from the Board.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.070) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.06 FIRES.
   (A)   No person shall start a fire in any park except for fires for eating
purposes in park grills. Privately-owned grills may only be used in areas
adjacent to shelter houses.
   (B)   All fires shall be put out by the person or persons who started or are
using the same before leaving the immediate vicinity of the fire.
   (C)   The dumping of hot ashes or fire from portable grills onto the grass
or plants is prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.050) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.07 SMOKING AND LITTERING PROHIBITED.
   (A)   Smoking. All of the following acts are hereby declared unlawful and a
violation when committed or caused to be committed by any person or groups of
persons within the boundaries or upon the lands of any park owned or operated
by the city, except for in the parking areas located within said parks:
      (1)   Smoking any cigarettes, cigars, pipes, other tobacco products or
other smokable products; or
      (2)   Littering any city-owned real estate by placing tobacco products or
tobacco containers on the ground of any part of real estate owned by the city.
   (B)   Littering. No person shall drop, cast or spill litter on park property
except for in receptacles provided for such purpose.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.060)
(Ord. 2011-05, passed 10-3-2011) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.08 ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES PROHIBITED.
   No person shall bring, have, carry, serve or drink alcoholic beverages
within the parks.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.020) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.09 DISORDERLY CONDUCT.
   (A)   No person shall, either by word or act, indulge in any noisy,
boisterous, disorderly or indecent conduct, nor in any manner so as to disturb
the peace or good order of the community within the parks.
   (B)   No person shall engage in any active game endangering other persons in
the parks.
   (C)   No person shall drink intoxicating liquor or be drunk, partake in any
form of gambling or do any indecent, lascivious, lewd or improper act therein.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.080) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.10 TRAFFIC AND PARKING.
   (A)   No person shall drive or propel, or cause to be driven or propelled,
any vehicle at a greater rate of speed than ten mph along or over any road
within the parks.
   (B)   Paths established for pedestrians and non- motorized vehicles shall
not be used by motorized vehicles.
   (C)   No person shall park any motorcar, motorcycle or other vehicle within
the parks except for in places designated for parking.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.090) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.11 BRINGING DOGS AND CATS.
   No dog, cat or any animal destructive to wildlife is permitted in the parks
unless said animal is controlled at all times on a leash not more than eight
feet long.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.120) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.12 FIREWORKS, FIREARMS AND WEAPONS.
   No person shall possess or discharge any firearms, fireworks or other
weapons within the parks without a permit from the Board.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.130) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.13 COMMERCIAL ENTERPRISES.
   No person shall sell or offer for sale any article, thing, privilege or
service within the parks without a permit from the Board.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.100) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.14 COMMERCIAL ADVERTISEMENTS.
   No person shall distribute or place commercial advertisements within the
parks without a permit from the Board
(Prior Code, § 8.42.110) Penalty, see §
96.99
BLACKFORD HIGH SCHOOL TRAIL
§ 96.25 USAGE REGULATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS.
   (A)   The following regulations shall be in full force and effect with
respect to the portion of Blackford High School Trail lying north of Park
Avenue within the limits of the incorporated city.
   (B)   The regulations are as follows.
      (1)   Parking is only permitted in designated parking areas, and no
parking is allowed along streets, highways or roadways.
      (2)   Trail hours are from dawn until dusk seven days a week, and use of
the trail outside of these hours is prohibited.
      (3)   Users of the trail do so at their own risk.
      (4)   Those using the trail must stop at all crossroads and must obey all
signage.
      (5)   Users must remove all trash and waste from the trail and the
property of adjoining landowners.
      (6)   The only animals allowed on the trail are pets which are kept on a
leash. Pets must be kept off of private property, and owners must clean up
after their pets and must not throw animal waste or other trash onto adjoining
landowners’s property.
      (7)   All motorized vehicles are prohibited on the trail, including
scooters, snowmobiles, all-terrain vehicles, golf carts, go-karts and other
similar motorized vehicles. E-bikes and peddle-assisted bikes are allowed on
the trail as long as they do not exceed a speed of 15 mph.
      (8)   Electric personal assistive mobility devices which are a single
passenger, self-balancing mode of transport with a maximum speed of 15 mph are
permitted on the trail.
      (9)   No person on the trail shall be in possession of or under the
influence of alcoholic beverages or illegal substances.
      (10)   No overnight camping or campfires are allowed on the trail.
      (11)   Due to the hazard for creating fires, smoking is prohibited on the
trail.
      (12)   No firearms, explosives, destructive devices or fireworks are
permitted on the trail.
      (13)   Hunting is prohibited on the trail.
      (14)   Vandalizing or intentional destruction or damage to the trail or
to any improvements located along the trail is a crime which shall be referred
to the County Prosecutor, and the city will pursue recovery of the cost of
repair or replacement from the offender.
(Ord. 2018-11, passed 12-3-2018) Penalty, see §
96.99
§ 96.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   General penalty. Any person violating any provision of this chapter
for which no specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99 of this code of ordinances.
   (B)   Parks and pools.
      (1)   Any person violating any of the provisions and regulations of §§
96.01 through
96.14 of this chapter shall be assessed a civil penalty as set forth in §
32.07 of this code for each violation.
(Prior Code, § 8.42.140)
      (2)   Any person or groups of persons who shall commit a violation of any
provision of §
96.07(B) of this chapter shall have imposed upon them a fine of not less than
$50 and not more than $500. Each and every incident or commission by a person
or groups of persons or causing of said commission shall constitute an
individual violation.
   (C)   Blackford High School Trail. A violation of any of the provisions of §
96.25 of this chapter shall be punishable by a fine in the sum of $50 for a
first violation and $100 for each additional violation. Each day any violation
of §
96.25 of this chapter shall continue shall constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. 2006-02, passed 6-5-2006; Ord. 2011-05, passed 10-3-2011; Ord. 2018-11,
passed 12-3-2018)

CHAPTER 110: REGULATIONS BY PROFESSION
